Please wait ${retryAfter} seconds.`,\n \"warning\",\n );\n\n // Optional: Auto-retry after delay\n if (options.autoRetry) {\n await sleep(retryAfter * 1000);\n return makeApiCall(url, options);\n }\n\n throw new Error(\"Rate limit exceeded\");\n }\n\n return response.json();\n } catch (error) {\n console.error(\"API call failed:\", error);\n throw error;\n }\n}\n```\n\n**Exponential Backoff:**\n\n\u0110\u1ed1i v\u1edbi automated clients, implement exponential backoff:\n\n```javascript\nasync function fetchWithRetry(url, maxRetries = 3) {\n for (let i = 0; i < maxRetries; i++) {\n try {\n const response = await fetch(url);\n\n if (response.ok) {\n return response.json();\n }\n\n if (response.status === 429) {\n const retryAfter = parseInt(\n response.headers.get(\"Retry-After\") || \"60\",\n );\n\n // Exponential backoff with jitter\n const delay = retryAfter * 1000 * Math.pow(2, i) + Math.random() * 1000;\n\n console.log(`Rate limited. Retrying in ${delay}ms...`);\n await sleep(delay);\n continue;\n }\n\n throw new Error(`HTTP ${response.status}`);\n } catch (error) {\n if (i === maxRetries - 1) throw error;\n }\n }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Takeaways\n\n1. **Rate limiting l\u00e0 essential** - Kh\u00f4ng ph\u1ea3i optional feature, m\u00e0 l\u00e0 core requirement cho production APIs\n\n2. **Ch\u1ecdn strategy ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p:**\n - Fixed window: \u0110\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n nh\u1ea5t, OK cho basic use cases\n - Sliding window: Ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c h\u01a1n, t\u1ed1t cho most applications\n - Token bucket: T\u1ed1t nh\u1ea5t cho variable load, cho ph\u00e9p bursts h\u1ee3p l\u00fd\n - Leaky bucket: T\u1ed1t cho protecting downstream services v\u1edbi strict rate requirements\n\n3. **Use Redis cho distributed systems** - \u0110\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o consistency across multiple instances\n\n4. **Lu\u00f4n return proper headers:**\n - `X-RateLimit-Limit`\n - `X-RateLimit-Remaining`\n - `X-RateLimit-Reset`\n - `Retry-After` (khi status 429)\n\n5. **Error handling quan tr\u1ecdng:**\n - Status 429 v\u1edbi clear message\n - Provide retry timing information\n - Documentation links\n\n6. **Think about UX** - Rate limiting kh\u00f4ng ch\u1ec9 l\u00e0 technical feature, m\u00e0 \u1ea3nh h\u01b0\u1edfng \u0111\u1ebfn user experience. Balance gi\u1eefa security/resource protection v\u1edbi usability.\n\n## K\u1ebft Lu\u1eadn\n\nRate limiting l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng patterns quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t trong API design. N\u00f3 b\u1ea3o v\u1ec7 resources, \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o fair usage, v\u00e0 ng\u0103n ch\u1eb7n abuse - t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 \u0111\u1ec1u critical cho m\u1ed9t production system \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u00e0 scalable.\n\nStart with simple approach (fixed window ho\u1eb7c sliding window), monitor usage patterns, v\u00e0 evolve strategy c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n based on actual needs. V\u00e0 nh\u1edb r\u1eb1ng: rate limiting kh\u00f4ng ch\u1ec9 v\u1ec1 limiting - m\u00e0 v\u1ec1 enabling sustainable, fair, v\u00e0 reliable service cho t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 users.\n\n**Next steps:**\n\n- Implement rate limiting trong API hi\u1ec7n t\u1ea1i c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n\n- Monitor rate limit metrics (rejection rate, popular limits hit, etc.)\n- Document rate limits r\u00f5 r\u00e0ng cho API consumers\n- Consider different tiers (free, paid) v\u1edbi different limits\n- Set up alerts khi c\u00f3 unusual rate limit patterns\n\n**Resources:**\n\n- [RFC 6585 - HTTP Status Code 429](https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6585)\n- [Redis Rate Limiting Patterns](https://redis.io/docs/manual/patterns/rate-limiter/)\n- [Express Rate Limit Library](https://www.npmjs.com/package/express-rate-limit)\n"}], "grading": null}, {"id": "rate-limiting-without_skill", "prompt": "Turn detailed outline into blog post about API rate limiting", "eval_id": 5, "outputs": [{"name": "rate-limiting-english.md", "type": "text", "content": "# A Complete Guide to API Rate Limiting\n\nRate limiting is a critical technique in API design that controls how many requests a client can make within a specific time window. Whether you're building a public API or an internal service, implementing proper rate limiting ensures your system remains stable, fair, and cost-effective.\n\n## Why Rate Limit Your API?\n\n### Prevent Abuse\n\nWithout rate limits, malicious actors or poorly designed clients can overwhelm your API with excessive requests. Rate limiting acts as your first line of defense against denial-of-service attacks and accidental traffic spikes.\n\n### Protect Resources\n\nYour infrastructure has finite capacity. Database connections, CPU cycles, and memory are all limited resources. By throttling incoming requests, you ensure that your system stays within operational boundaries and maintains consistent performance for all users.\n\n### Fair Usage\n\nRate limiting ensures that no single user monopolizes your API. This creates a level playing field where all clients get their fair share of resources, preventing one high-volume user from degrading the experience for everyone else.\n\n### Cost Control\n\nMany APIs rely on third-party services or cloud resources that charge per request. Rate limiting helps you predict and control operational costs by capping the maximum throughput your system needs to handle.\n\n## Rate Limiting Strategies\n\nChoosing the right rate limiting algorithm depends on your use case. Here are the four most common strategies:\n\n### 1. Fixed Window\n\nThe fixed window algorithm is the simplest approach. It maintains a counter that tracks requests within fixed time intervals (e.g., every minute or hour). When the interval ends, the counter resets to zero.\n\n**How it works:**\n\n- Start counting at time 0\n- Increment counter for each request\n- Reset counter at the end of each window\n\n**Pros:**\n\n- Simple to implement\n- Low memory overhead\n- Easy to understand\n\n**Cons:**\n\n- Vulnerable to burst traffic at window edges\n- A user could make 2\u00d7 the limit by timing requests at window boundaries\n\n**Best for:** Simple applications where occasional bursts are acceptable.\n\n### 2. Sliding Window\n\nThe sliding window algorithm provides more accurate rate limiting by calculating the rate based on the previous window plus the current window. This smooths out the edge case problem of fixed windows.\n\n**How it works:**\n\n- Track requests in the current window\n- Calculate weighted contribution from previous window\n- Reject if combined count exceeds limit\n\n**Pros:**\n\n- More accurate than fixed window\n- Prevents burst attacks at window edges\n- Still relatively simple\n\n**Cons:**\n\n- Slightly more complex to implement\n- Requires storing data from previous window\n\n**Best for:** Production APIs where accuracy matters.\n\n### 3. Token Bucket\n\nThe token bucket algorithm allows controlled bursts while maintaining an average rate. Tokens are added to a bucket at a steady rate, and each request consumes a token. If the bucket is empty, requests are rejected.\n\n**How it works:**\n\n- Bucket holds tokens up to a maximum capacity\n- Tokens added at a constant rate\n- Each request consumes one token\n- Requests fail when bucket is empty\n\n**Pros:**\n\n- Allows legitimate bursts of traffic\n- Good for variable workloads\n- Flexible and configurable\n\n**Cons:**\n\n- More complex to implement correctly\n- Requires careful tuning of bucket size and refill rate\n\n**Best for:** APIs with variable load patterns and legitimate burst needs.\n\n### 4. Leaky Bucket\n\nThe leaky bucket algorithm processes requests at a constant rate, queueing excess requests in a bucket. Requests \"leak\" from the bucket at a steady rate. When the bucket overflows, new requests are rejected.\n\n**How it works:**\n\n- Requests enter a queue (bucket)\n- Requests processed at fixed rate\n- Queue has maximum size\n- Overflow requests are rejected\n\n**Pros:**\n\n- Smooths out traffic spikes\n- Predictable output rate\n- Protects downstream services\n\n**Cons:**\n\n- Adds latency due to queuing\n- Can accumulate stale requests\n- More complex than other approaches\n\n**Best for:** Systems requiring smooth, predictable load on backend services.\n\n## Implementation Guide\n\n### Choosing Your Storage Backend\n\n**Redis for Distributed Systems:**\n\n```javascript\nconst redis = require(\"redis\");\nconst client = redis.createClient();\n\nasync function checkRateLimit(userId, limit, windowSeconds) {\n const key = `rate_limit:${userId}`;\n const current = await client.incr(key);\n\n if (current === 1) {\n await client.expire(key, windowSeconds);\n }\n\n return current <= limit;\n}\n```\n\n**In-Memory for Single Server:**\n\n```javascript\nconst rateLimitMap = new Map();\n\nfunction checkRateLimit(userId, limit, windowMs) {\n const now = Date.now();\n const userLimit = rateLimitMap.get(userId) || {\n count: 0,\n resetTime: now + windowMs,\n };\n\n if (now > userLimit.resetTime) {\n userLimit.count = 0;\n userLimit.resetTime = now + windowMs;\n }\n\n userLimit.count++;\n rateLimitMap.set(userId, userLimit);\n\n return userLimit.count <= limit;\n}\n```\n\n### Express Middleware Example\n\n```javascript\nconst rateLimit = (limit, windowMs) => {\n return async (req, res, next) => {\n const userId = req.user?.id || req.ip;\n const key = `rate_limit:${userId}`;\n\n const current = await redis.incr(key);\n const ttl = await redis.ttl(key);\n\n if (ttl === -1) {\n await redis.expire(key, Math.floor(windowMs / 1000));\n }\n\n // Set rate limit headers\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Limit\", limit);\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Remaining\", Math.max(0, limit - current));\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Reset\", Date.now() + ttl * 1000);\n\n if (current > limit) {\n return res.status(429).json({\n error: \"Too Many Requests\",\n message: `Rate limit exceeded. Try again in ${ttl} seconds.`,\n });\n }\n\n next();\n };\n};\n\n// Usage\napp.use(\"/api/\", rateLimit(100, 60000)); // 100 requests per minute\n```\n\n### Rate Limit Headers\n\nStandard headers to include in your responses:\n\n- **X-RateLimit-Limit:** Maximum requests allowed in the window\n- **X-RateLimit-Remaining:** Requests remaining in current window\n- **X-RateLimit-Reset:** Unix timestamp when the limit resets\n\nThese headers help clients implement smart retry logic and avoid hitting limits.\n\n## Handling Rate Limit Violations\n\nWhen a user exceeds their rate limit, your API should respond appropriately:\n\n### Return 429 Status Code\n\nThe HTTP 429 \"Too Many Requests\" status code is the standard way to indicate rate limiting.\n\n```javascript\nres.status(429).json({\n error: \"Too Many Requests\",\n message: \"Rate limit exceeded\",\n});\n```\n\n### Include Retry-After Header\n\nTell clients when they can retry:\n\n```javascript\nres.setHeader(\"Retry-After\", 60); // seconds until reset\n```\n\n### Provide Clear Error Messages\n\nHelp developers debug rate limit issues:\n\n```javascript\n{\n \"error\": \"rate_limit_exceeded\",\n \"message\": \"You have exceeded the rate limit of 100 requests per minute.\",\n \"limit\": 100,\n \"remaining\": 0,\n \"reset\": 1648234560,\n \"reset_human\": \"2024-03-25T12:56:00Z\"\n}\n```\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Document your limits clearly** - Make rate limits visible in your API documentation\n2. **Use tiered limits** - Different limits for free vs. paid users\n3. **Implement gradually** - Start with generous limits and tighten as needed\n4. **Monitor and alert** - Track rate limit hits to identify issues\n5. **Provide upgrade paths** - Let users request higher limits when needed\n6. **Test thoroughly** - Ensure limits work correctly under various scenarios\n\n## Conclusion\n\nRate limiting is essential for building robust, fair, and scalable APIs. Start with a simple fixed window approach for basic needs, then graduate to sliding windows or token buckets as your requirements grow. Remember to communicate limits clearly through headers and documentation, and always provide helpful error messages when limits are exceeded.\n\nThe investment in proper rate limiting pays dividends in system stability, fair resource distribution, and happier users. Your API\u2014and your infrastructure team\u2014will thank you.\n"}, {"name": "rate-limiting-vietnamese.md", "type": "text", "content": "# H\u01b0\u1edbng D\u1eabn To\u00e0n Di\u1ec7n V\u1ec1 Rate Limiting Cho API\n\nRate limiting l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t k\u1ef9 thu\u1eadt quan tr\u1ecdng trong thi\u1ebft k\u1ebf API, gi\u00fap ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t s\u1ed1 l\u01b0\u1ee3ng request m\u00e0 m\u1ed9t client c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 g\u1eedi trong m\u1ed9t kho\u1ea3ng th\u1eddi gian nh\u1ea5t \u0111\u1ecbnh. D\u00f9 b\u1ea1n \u0111ang x\u00e2y d\u1ef1ng API public hay internal service, vi\u1ec7c tri\u1ec3n khai rate limiting \u0111\u00fang c\u00e1ch s\u1ebd \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh, c\u00f4ng b\u1eb1ng v\u00e0 ti\u1ebft ki\u1ec7m chi ph\u00ed.\n\n## T\u1ea1i Sao C\u1ea7n Rate Limiting?\n\n### Ng\u0103n Ch\u1eb7n L\u1ea1m D\u1ee5ng\n\nKh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 rate limiting, c\u00e1c tin t\u1eb7c ho\u1eb7c client \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c thi\u1ebft k\u1ebf k\u00e9m c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 l\u00e0m qu\u00e1 t\u1ea3i API c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n v\u1edbi s\u1ed1 l\u01b0\u1ee3ng request kh\u1ed5ng l\u1ed3. Rate limiting \u0111\u00f3ng vai tr\u00f2 l\u00e0 tuy\u1ebfn ph\u00f2ng th\u1ee7 \u0111\u1ea7u ti\u00ean ch\u1ed1ng l\u1ea1i c\u00e1c cu\u1ed9c t\u1ea5n c\u00f4ng denial-of-service v\u00e0 c\u00e1c \u0111\u1ee3t t\u0103ng traffic b\u1ea5t th\u01b0\u1eddng.\n\n### B\u1ea3o V\u1ec7 T\u00e0i Nguy\u00ean\n\nH\u1ea1 t\u1ea7ng c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 n\u0103ng l\u1ef1c gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n. K\u1ebft n\u1ed1i database, CPU, v\u00e0 b\u1ed9 nh\u1edb \u0111\u1ec1u l\u00e0 t\u00e0i nguy\u00ean h\u1eefu h\u1ea1n. B\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n request \u0111\u1ebfn, b\u1ea1n \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng trong gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n an to\u00e0n v\u00e0 duy tr\u00ec hi\u1ec7u su\u1ea5t \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh cho t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng.\n\n### S\u1eed D\u1ee5ng C\u00f4ng B\u1eb1ng\n\nRate limiting \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 user n\u00e0o \u0111\u1ed9c chi\u1ebfm API c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y t\u1ea1o ra s\u00e2n ch\u01a1i b\u00ecnh \u0111\u1eb3ng, n\u01a1i t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 c\u00e1c client \u0111\u1ec1u nh\u1eadn \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c ph\u1ea7n t\u00e0i nguy\u00ean c\u00f4ng b\u1eb1ng, ng\u0103n kh\u00f4ng cho m\u1ed9t user c\u00f3 l\u01b0u l\u01b0\u1ee3ng cao l\u00e0m gi\u1ea3m tr\u1ea3i nghi\u1ec7m c\u1ee7a nh\u1eefng ng\u01b0\u1eddi kh\u00e1c.\n\n### Ki\u1ec3m So\u00e1t Chi Ph\u00ed\n\nNhi\u1ec1u API d\u1ef1a v\u00e0o c\u00e1c d\u1ecbch v\u1ee5 b\u00ean th\u1ee9 ba ho\u1eb7c t\u00e0i nguy\u00ean cloud t\u00ednh ph\u00ed theo request. Rate limiting gi\u00fap b\u1ea1n d\u1ef1 \u0111o\u00e1n v\u00e0 ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t chi ph\u00ed v\u1eadn h\u00e0nh b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n throughput t\u1ed1i \u0111a m\u00e0 h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng c\u1ea7n x\u1eed l\u00fd.\n\n## C\u00e1c Chi\u1ebfn L\u01b0\u1ee3c Rate Limiting\n\nL\u1ef1a ch\u1ecdn thu\u1eadt to\u00e1n rate limiting ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p ph\u1ee5 thu\u1ed9c v\u00e0o use case c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n. D\u01b0\u1edbi \u0111\u00e2y l\u00e0 b\u1ed1n chi\u1ebfn l\u01b0\u1ee3c ph\u1ed5 bi\u1ebfn nh\u1ea5t:\n\n### 1. Fixed Window (C\u1eeda S\u1ed5 C\u1ed1 \u0110\u1ecbnh)\n\nThu\u1eadt to\u00e1n fixed window l\u00e0 c\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n nh\u1ea5t. N\u00f3 duy tr\u00ec m\u1ed9t b\u1ed9 \u0111\u1ebfm theo d\u00f5i request trong c\u00e1c kho\u1ea3ng th\u1eddi gian c\u1ed1 \u0111\u1ecbnh (v\u00ed d\u1ee5: m\u1ed7i ph\u00fat ho\u1eb7c m\u1ed7i gi\u1edd). Khi kho\u1ea3ng th\u1eddi gian k\u1ebft th\u00fac, b\u1ed9 \u0111\u1ebfm reset v\u1ec1 0.\n\n**C\u00e1ch ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng:**\n\n- B\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u \u0111\u1ebfm t\u1ea1i th\u1eddi \u0111i\u1ec3m 0\n- T\u0103ng b\u1ed9 \u0111\u1ebfm cho m\u1ed7i request\n- Reset b\u1ed9 \u0111\u1ebfm khi k\u1ebft th\u00fac m\u1ed7i window\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- \u0110\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n \u0111\u1ec3 tri\u1ec3n khai\n- \u00cdt t\u1ed1n b\u1ed9 nh\u1edb\n- D\u1ec5 hi\u1ec3u\n\n**Nh\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- D\u1ec5 b\u1ecb t\u1ea5n c\u00f4ng burst traffic t\u1ea1i bi\u00ean c\u1ee7a window\n- User c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 g\u1eedi g\u1ea5p \u0111\u00f4i gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch t\u00ednh to\u00e1n th\u1eddi \u0111i\u1ec3m t\u1ea1i bi\u00ean window\n\n**Ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p cho:** \u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 ch\u1ea5p nh\u1eadn burst th\u1ec9nh tho\u1ea3ng.\n\n### 2. Sliding Window (C\u1eeda S\u1ed5 Tr\u01b0\u1ee3t)\n\nThu\u1eadt to\u00e1n sliding window cung c\u1ea5p rate limiting ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c h\u01a1n b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch t\u00ednh to\u00e1n rate d\u1ef1a tr\u00ean window tr\u01b0\u1edbc \u0111\u00f3 c\u1ed9ng v\u1edbi window hi\u1ec7n t\u1ea1i. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y gi\u1ea3i quy\u1ebft v\u1ea5n \u0111\u1ec1 edge case c\u1ee7a fixed window.\n\n**C\u00e1ch ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng:**\n\n- Theo d\u00f5i request trong window hi\u1ec7n t\u1ea1i\n- T\u00ednh to\u00e1n weighted contribution t\u1eeb window tr\u01b0\u1edbc\n- T\u1eeb ch\u1ed1i n\u1ebfu t\u1ed5ng s\u1ed1 v\u01b0\u1ee3t gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c h\u01a1n fixed window\n- Ng\u0103n ch\u1eb7n t\u1ea5n c\u00f4ng burst t\u1ea1i bi\u00ean window\n- V\u1eabn t\u01b0\u01a1ng \u0111\u1ed1i \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n\n\n**Nh\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Ph\u1ee9c t\u1ea1p h\u01a1n m\u1ed9t ch\u00fat \u0111\u1ec3 tri\u1ec3n khai\n- C\u1ea7n l\u01b0u tr\u1eef d\u1eef li\u1ec7u t\u1eeb window tr\u01b0\u1edbc\n\n**Ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p cho:** Production API n\u01a1i \u0111\u1ed9 ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c quan tr\u1ecdng.\n\n### 3. Token Bucket (Th\u00f9ng Token)\n\nThu\u1eadt to\u00e1n token bucket cho ph\u00e9p burst c\u00f3 ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t trong khi duy tr\u00ec average rate. Token \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c th\u00eam v\u00e0o th\u00f9ng v\u1edbi t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh, v\u00e0 m\u1ed7i request ti\u00eau th\u1ee5 m\u1ed9t token. N\u1ebfu th\u00f9ng r\u1ed7ng, request b\u1ecb t\u1eeb ch\u1ed1i.\n\n**C\u00e1ch ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng:**\n\n- Th\u00f9ng ch\u1ee9a token \u0111\u1ebfn s\u1ee9c ch\u1ee9a t\u1ed1i \u0111a\n- Token \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c th\u00eam v\u1edbi t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 c\u1ed1 \u0111\u1ecbnh\n- M\u1ed7i request ti\u00eau th\u1ee5 m\u1ed9t token\n- Request th\u1ea5t b\u1ea1i khi th\u00f9ng r\u1ed7ng\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Cho ph\u00e9p burst traffic h\u1ee3p l\u1ec7\n- T\u1ed1t cho workload bi\u1ebfn \u0111\u1ed5i\n- Linh ho\u1ea1t v\u00e0 c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 c\u1ea5u h\u00ecnh\n\n**Nh\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Ph\u1ee9c t\u1ea1p h\u01a1n \u0111\u1ec3 tri\u1ec3n khai \u0111\u00fang\n- C\u1ea7n \u0111i\u1ec1u ch\u1ec9nh c\u1ea9n th\u1eadn k\u00edch th\u01b0\u1edbc th\u00f9ng v\u00e0 t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 refill\n\n**Ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p cho:** API c\u00f3 pattern t\u1ea3i bi\u1ebfn \u0111\u1ed5i v\u00e0 nhu c\u1ea7u burst h\u1ee3p l\u1ec7.\n\n### 4. Leaky Bucket (Th\u00f9ng D\u1ed9t)\n\nThu\u1eadt to\u00e1n leaky bucket x\u1eed l\u00fd request v\u1edbi t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 c\u1ed1 \u0111\u1ecbnh, x\u1ebfp h\u00e0ng c\u00e1c request d\u01b0 th\u1eeba trong m\u1ed9t th\u00f9ng. Request \"r\u00f2 r\u1ec9\" t\u1eeb th\u00f9ng v\u1edbi t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh. Khi th\u00f9ng tr\u00e0n, request m\u1edbi b\u1ecb t\u1eeb ch\u1ed1i.\n\n**C\u00e1ch ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng:**\n\n- Request v\u00e0o h\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ee3i (th\u00f9ng)\n- Request \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c x\u1eed l\u00fd v\u1edbi t\u1ed1c \u0111\u1ed9 c\u1ed1 \u0111\u1ecbnh\n- H\u00e0ng \u0111\u1ee3i c\u00f3 k\u00edch th\u01b0\u1edbc t\u1ed1i \u0111a\n- Request tr\u00e0n b\u1ecb t\u1eeb ch\u1ed1i\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- L\u00e0m m\u01b0\u1ee3t c\u00e1c \u0111\u1ee3t t\u0103ng traffic\n- Output rate c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 d\u1ef1 \u0111o\u00e1n\n- B\u1ea3o v\u1ec7 c\u00e1c service downstream\n\n**Nh\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Th\u00eam \u0111\u1ed9 tr\u1ec5 do queuing\n- C\u00f3 th\u1ec3 t\u00edch l\u0169y request c\u0169\n- Ph\u1ee9c t\u1ea1p h\u01a1n c\u00e1c c\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn kh\u00e1c\n\n**Ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p cho:** H\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng y\u00eau c\u1ea7u t\u1ea3i m\u01b0\u1ee3t v\u00e0 c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 d\u1ef1 \u0111o\u00e1n tr\u00ean backend service.\n\n## H\u01b0\u1edbng D\u1eabn Tri\u1ec3n Khai\n\n### Ch\u1ecdn Storage Backend\n\n**Redis cho H\u1ec7 Th\u1ed1ng Ph\u00e2n T\u00e1n:**\n\n```javascript\nconst redis = require(\"redis\");\nconst client = redis.createClient();\n\nasync function checkRateLimit(userId, limit, windowSeconds) {\n const key = `rate_limit:${userId}`;\n const current = await client.incr(key);\n\n if (current === 1) {\n await client.expire(key, windowSeconds);\n }\n\n return current <= limit;\n}\n```\n\n**In-Memory cho Single Server:**\n\n```javascript\nconst rateLimitMap = new Map();\n\nfunction checkRateLimit(userId, limit, windowMs) {\n const now = Date.now();\n const userLimit = rateLimitMap.get(userId) || {\n count: 0,\n resetTime: now + windowMs,\n };\n\n if (now > userLimit.resetTime) {\n userLimit.count = 0;\n userLimit.resetTime = now + windowMs;\n }\n\n userLimit.count++;\n rateLimitMap.set(userId, userLimit);\n\n return userLimit.count <= limit;\n}\n```\n\n### V\u00ed D\u1ee5 Express Middleware\n\n```javascript\nconst rateLimit = (limit, windowMs) => {\n return async (req, res, next) => {\n const userId = req.user?.id || req.ip;\n const key = `rate_limit:${userId}`;\n\n const current = await redis.incr(key);\n const ttl = await redis.ttl(key);\n\n if (ttl === -1) {\n await redis.expire(key, Math.floor(windowMs / 1000));\n }\n\n // Set rate limit headers\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Limit\", limit);\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Remaining\", Math.max(0, limit - current));\n res.setHeader(\"X-RateLimit-Reset\", Date.now() + ttl * 1000);\n\n if (current > limit) {\n return res.status(429).json({\n error: \"Too Many Requests\",\n message: `V\u01b0\u1ee3t gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n rate. Th\u1eed l\u1ea1i sau ${ttl} gi\u00e2y.`,\n });\n }\n\n next();\n };\n};\n\n// S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng\napp.use(\"/api/\", rateLimit(100, 60000)); // 100 request m\u1ed7i ph\u00fat\n```\n\n### Rate Limit Headers\n\nC\u00e1c header chu\u1ea9n c\u1ea7n include trong response:\n\n- **X-RateLimit-Limit:** S\u1ed1 request t\u1ed1i \u0111a cho ph\u00e9p trong window\n- **X-RateLimit-Remaining:** S\u1ed1 request c\u00f2n l\u1ea1i trong window hi\u1ec7n t\u1ea1i\n- **X-RateLimit-Reset:** Unix timestamp khi limit \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c reset\n\nC\u00e1c header n\u00e0y gi\u00fap client tri\u1ec3n khai retry logic th\u00f4ng minh v\u00e0 tr\u00e1nh v\u01b0\u1ee3t limit.\n\n## X\u1eed L\u00fd Khi Vi Ph\u1ea1m Rate Limit\n\nKhi user v\u01b0\u1ee3t qu\u00e1 rate limit, API c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n c\u1ea7n ph\u1ea3n h\u1ed3i th\u00edch h\u1ee3p:\n\n### Tr\u1ea3 V\u1ec1 Status Code 429\n\nHTTP 429 \"Too Many Requests\" l\u00e0 status code chu\u1ea9n \u0111\u1ec3 ch\u1ec9 ra rate limiting.\n\n```javascript\nres.status(429).json({\n error: \"Too Many Requests\",\n message: \"V\u01b0\u1ee3t gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n rate\",\n});\n```\n\n### Include Retry-After Header\n\nCho client bi\u1ebft khi n\u00e0o c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 retry:\n\n```javascript\nres.setHeader(\"Retry-After\", 60); // gi\u00e2y cho \u0111\u1ebfn khi reset\n```\n\n### Cung C\u1ea5p Error Message R\u00f5 R\u00e0ng\n\nGi\u00fap developer debug v\u1ea5n \u0111\u1ec1 rate limit:\n\n```javascript\n{\n \"error\": \"rate_limit_exceeded\",\n \"message\": \"B\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 v\u01b0\u1ee3t gi\u1edbi h\u1ea1n rate l\u00e0 100 request m\u1ed7i ph\u00fat.\",\n \"limit\": 100,\n \"remaining\": 0,\n \"reset\": 1648234560,\n \"reset_human\": \"2024-03-25T12:56:00Z\"\n}\n```\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Document limit r\u00f5 r\u00e0ng** - L\u00e0m cho rate limit hi\u1ec3n th\u1ecb trong t\u00e0i li\u1ec7u API\n2. **S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng tiered limit** - Limit kh\u00e1c nhau cho user free vs. paid\n3. **Tri\u1ec3n khai t\u1eeb t\u1eeb** - B\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u v\u1edbi limit r\u1ed9ng r\u00e3i v\u00e0 th\u1eaft ch\u1eb7t d\u1ea7n khi c\u1ea7n\n4. **Monitor v\u00e0 alert** - Theo d\u00f5i rate limit hit \u0111\u1ec3 x\u00e1c \u0111\u1ecbnh v\u1ea5n \u0111\u1ec1\n5. **Cung c\u1ea5p upgrade path** - Cho ph\u00e9p user y\u00eau c\u1ea7u limit cao h\u01a1n khi c\u1ea7n\n6. **Test k\u1ef9 l\u01b0\u1ee1ng** - \u0110\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o limit ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng \u0111\u00fang trong nhi\u1ec1u scenario\n\n## K\u1ebft Lu\u1eadn\n\nRate limiting l\u00e0 thi\u1ebft y\u1ebfu \u0111\u1ec3 x\u00e2y d\u1ef1ng API m\u1ea1nh m\u1ebd, c\u00f4ng b\u1eb1ng v\u00e0 c\u00f3 kh\u1ea3 n\u0103ng m\u1edf r\u1ed9ng. B\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u v\u1edbi c\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn fixed window \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n cho nhu c\u1ea7u c\u01a1 b\u1ea3n, sau \u0111\u00f3 n\u00e2ng c\u1ea5p l\u00ean sliding window ho\u1eb7c token bucket khi y\u00eau c\u1ea7u t\u0103ng l\u00ean. Nh\u1edb truy\u1ec1n \u0111\u1ea1t limit r\u00f5 r\u00e0ng qua header v\u00e0 t\u00e0i li\u1ec7u, v\u00e0 lu\u00f4n cung c\u1ea5p error message h\u1eefu \u00edch khi limit b\u1ecb v\u01b0\u1ee3t.\n\n\u0110\u1ea7u t\u01b0 v\u00e0o rate limiting \u0111\u00fang c\u00e1ch s\u1ebd mang l\u1ea1i l\u1ee3i \u00edch v\u1ec1 t\u00ednh \u1ed5n \u0111\u1ecbnh h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng, ph\u00e2n ph\u1ed1i t\u00e0i nguy\u00ean c\u00f4ng b\u1eb1ng, v\u00e0 user h\u00e0i l\u00f2ng h\u01a1n. API c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n\u2014v\u00e0 team infrastructure\u2014s\u1ebd c\u1ea3m \u01a1n b\u1ea1n.\n"}], "grading": null}, {"id": "git-rebase-merge-with_skill", "prompt": "Transform casual notes about git rebase vs merge into professional blog post", "eval_id": 6, "outputs": [{"name": "blog-post-en.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Git Rebase vs Merge: Choosing the Right Strategy for Your Workflow\n\n> **For developers who want to master git history and collaboration best practices**\n\nHave you ever looked at your project's git history and found it to be a tangled mess of merge commits? Or conversely, have you accidentally rebased a public branch and caused chaos for your entire team? Choosing between `git merge` and `git rebase` is one of the most important decisions that impacts code collaboration.\n\nIn this article, we'll dive deep into how merge and rebase work, when to use each, and the best practices to avoid common pitfalls.\n\n## Part 1: Understanding Git Merge\n\n### 1.1 How Does Merge Work?\n\nGit merge creates a new **merge commit** that combines two branches together. This merge commit has two parent commits - one from the current branch and one from the branch being merged in.\n\n```bash\n# Merge feature branch into main\ngit checkout main\ngit merge feature-branch\n```\n\n**Result in git history:**\n\n```\n A---B---C feature-branch\n / \\\nD---E---F---G---M main\n```\n\nCommit `M` is the merge commit that connects the history of both branches.\n\n### 1.2 Advantages of Merge\n\n**Preserves complete history:**\n\n- All commits remain unchanged\n- Full context about when and how changes were integrated\n- Easy to trace back through the development process\n\n**Safe for team collaboration:**\n\n- Doesn't modify existing commits\n- No conflicts with what's already pushed to remote\n- Transparent - everyone can see merge points\n\n```bash\n# Safe workflow for teams\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit merge main # Sync with latest main\ngit push origin feature-branch\n```\n\n### 1.3 Disadvantages of Merge\n\n**History can become cluttered:**\n\n```\n* Merge branch 'feature-1' into main\n|\\\n| * Fix typo\n| * Add tests\n| * Implement feature\n* | Merge branch 'feature-2' into main\n|\\|\n| * Another fix\n| * Some work\n* | Merge branch 'hotfix' into main\n```\n\nWith multiple features being developed in parallel, git history can become difficult to read and understand the main development flow.\n\n## Part 2: Understanding Git Rebase\n\n### 2.1 How Does Rebase Work?\n\nGit rebase **rewrites history** by reapplying your commits on top of a new base commit. Instead of creating a merge commit, rebase moves your entire feature branch to the tip of the target branch.\n\n```bash\n# Rebase feature branch onto main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit rebase main\n```\n\n**Before rebase:**\n\n```\n A---B---C feature-branch\n /\nD---E---F---G main\n```\n\n**After rebase:**\n\n```\n A'---B'---C' feature-branch\n /\nD---E---F---G main\n```\n\nNote: `A'`, `B'`, `C'` are **new** commits with different SHAs, even though their content matches `A`, `B`, `C`.\n\n### 2.2 Advantages of Rebase\n\n**Linear history - clean and readable:**\n\n```bash\n# Linear history after rebase\nD---E---F---G---A---B---C\n```\n\nNo merge commits, everything in a straight line. When reading git log, you see exactly the sequence in which changes were implemented.\n\n**Very clean git log:**\n\n```bash\n$ git log --oneline\nc3d2a1f (HEAD -> feature-branch) Add comprehensive tests\nb8e9f0c Implement user authentication\na7d6c5b Update dependencies\nf9e8d7c Merge pull request #42\n```\n\nCompared to a log filled with merge commits, linear history makes it much easier to understand project evolution.\n\n### 2.3 Interactive Rebase - Powerful Tool\n\nOne of the most powerful features of rebase is **interactive mode**:\n\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3\n```\n\nThis opens an editor allowing you to:\n\n```\npick a7d6c5b Implement feature\npick b8e9f0c Fix bug\npick c3d2a1f Add tests\n\n# Commands:\n# p, pick = use commit\n# r, reword = use commit, but edit message\n# e, edit = use commit, but stop for amending\n# s, squash = meld into previous commit\n# f, fixup = like squash, but discard message\n# d, drop = remove commit\n```\n\n**Common use cases:**\n\n**1. Squash commits before PR:**\n\n```bash\n# Instead of:\n- WIP: initial work\n- Fix typo\n- Fix another typo\n- Actually fix the thing\n- Add tests\n\n# Becomes:\n- Implement user authentication with tests\n```\n\n**2. Reorder commits logically:**\n\n```bash\n# Reorganize commits by logic:\n- Add database migration\n- Update models\n- Add API endpoints\n- Add tests\n```\n\n**3. Clean up commit messages:**\n\n```bash\n# From: \"fixed stuff\" \"ugh why\" \"this works now\"\n# To: \"Refactor authentication flow\"\n \"Add comprehensive error handling\"\n \"Improve test coverage\"\n```\n\n## Part 3: When to Use Merge vs Rebase?\n\n### 3.1 The Golden Rule of Rebase\n\n> **NEVER REBASE PUBLIC BRANCHES**\n\nThis is the most important rule. If your branch has been pushed to remote and others might be working on it, **don't rebase**.\n\n**Why?** Because rebase creates new commits with new SHAs. If someone has already pulled the old branch, their history will conflict with your rebased version:\n\n```\nYour teammate's local: Your rebased version:\nA---B---C A'---B'---C'\n\n# Git sees these as diverged branches!\n```\n\nResult: conflicts, confusion, and potentially lost code.\n\n### 3.2 Merge - Safe for Shared Branches\n\n**Use MERGE when:**\n\n\u2705 Integrating shared branches (main \u2190 feature)\n\u2705 Branch has been published/pushed to remote\n\u2705 Working in a team (multiple people on same branch)\n\u2705 Need to preserve full context and history\n\u2705 Uncertain about who else is working on the branch\n\n**Typical workflow:**\n\n```bash\n# Feature development complete\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit merge feature-branch\ngit push origin main\n```\n\n### 3.3 Rebase - Good for Local Feature Branches\n\n**Use REBASE when:**\n\n\u2705 Cleaning up local commits before PR\n\u2705 Your branch hasn't been shared with anyone\n\u2705 Want linear history\n\u2705 Syncing feature branch with latest main\n\u2705 Feature branch development (before pushing)\n\n**Typical workflow:**\n\n```bash\n# Keep feature branch updated with main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# Clean up commits before PR\ngit rebase -i HEAD~5\n\n# Now push (first time or with --force-with-lease)\ngit push origin feature-branch --force-with-lease\n```\n\n### 3.4 Git Pull Rebase - Best Practice\n\nWhen pulling changes from remote, you have two options:\n\n```bash\n# Default: merge (creates merge commit)\ngit pull origin main\n\n# Rebase: linear history\ngit pull --rebase origin main\n# Or\ngit config pull.rebase true # Set as default\n```\n\n**Git pull --rebase workflow:**\n\n```\n# Before pull:\n Your local work\n D---E (local main)\n /\nA---B---C (remote main)\n\n# After git pull --rebase:\nA---B---C---D'---E' (main)\n```\n\nThis keeps history linear and avoids unnecessary merge commits from syncing with remote.\n\n## Part 4: Best Practices and Common Pitfalls\n\n### 4.1 Feature Branch Workflow\n\n**Recommended approach:**\n\n```bash\n# 1. Start feature branch from main\ngit checkout -b feature/user-auth main\n\n# 2. Make commits as you work\ngit commit -m \"Add login endpoint\"\ngit commit -m \"Add password hashing\"\ngit commit -m \"Add tests\"\n\n# 3. Periodically sync with main (rebase while still private)\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# 4. Clean up commits before PR\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3 # Squash/reorganize\n\n# 5. Push to remote\ngit push origin feature/user-auth\n\n# 6. Create PR - from this point use MERGE\n# After PR approved:\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main # Should include your merged PR\n```\n\n### 4.2 Safety with --force-with-lease\n\nIf you've rebased a branch that's already been pushed, you'll need to force push. **Never use `--force`**, always use `--force-with-lease`:\n\n```bash\n# \u274c DANGEROUS\ngit push --force\n\n# \u2705 SAFER\ngit push --force-with-lease origin feature-branch\n```\n\n`--force-with-lease` only force pushes if the remote branch hasn't been updated since you last fetched. This protects against accidentally overwriting work from teammates.\n\n### 4.3 Recovery From Rebase Mistakes\n\nIf a rebase goes wrong, **don't panic**:\n\n```bash\n# Git keeps a reference log of all operations\ngit reflog\n\n# Output:\n# c3d2a1f HEAD@{0}: rebase finished\n# a7d6c5b HEAD@{1}: rebase: Add tests\n# f9e8d7c HEAD@{2}: checkout: moving from main to feature\n\n# Reset to state before rebase\ngit reset --hard HEAD@{2}\n```\n\nGit reflog is your safety net - it tracks all changes to HEAD, allowing you to undo almost anything.\n\n### 4.4 Quick Comparison\n\n| Criteria | Merge | Rebase |\n| :--------------- | :-------------------------------- | :------------------------------------ |\n| **History** | Preserves all commits and context | Linear, cleaner history |\n| **Safety** | Very safe, no history rewriting | Requires caution with public branches |\n| **Teamwork** | Ideal for collaboration | Good for solo feature work |\n| **Traceability** | Full context with merge points | Context can be lost |\n| **Complexity** | Simpler, straightforward | More powerful, requires understanding |\n| **Use case** | Integrating shared branches | Cleaning up local work |\n\n## Part 5: When Both Are OK?\n\nIn practice, you often **combine both approaches**:\n\n```bash\n# Typical workflow combining both:\n\n# 1. Local feature development - use rebase freely\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3 # Clean up commits\ngit rebase main # Stay updated with main\n\n# 2. Before creating PR\ngit push origin feature-branch\n\n# 3. Team review and updates on PR\n# Other developers may add commits\ngit pull origin feature-branch # Now use merge!\n\n# 4. Final integration into main\n# Via PR merge (GitHub/GitLab handles this)\n# Most teams use \"Squash and merge\" or \"Rebase and merge\"\n```\n\n## Key Takeaways\n\n\u2705 **Merge creates merge commits** - safe, preserves history, good for team collaboration\n\n\u2705 **Rebase rewrites history** - creates linear history, cleaner log, good for feature branches\n\n\u274c **Never rebase public/shared branches** - will cause conflicts and confusion\n\n\u2705 **Rebase local feature branches** before pushing or creating PR - clean commit history\n\n\u2705 **Interactive rebase (`-i`)** is a powerful tool to clean up commits, reorder, squash\n\n\u2705 **Use `git pull --rebase`** to avoid unnecessary merge commits\n\n\u2705 **`--force-with-lease`** is safer than `--force` when force pushing is needed\n\n\u2705 **Merge for integration**, **rebase for refinement**\n\n## Conclusion\n\nChoosing between merge and rebase isn't an either/or decision - it's about understanding **when to use each approach**. Merge provides safety and full context, perfect for team collaboration and shared branches. Rebase gives you clean, linear history and powerful tools to refine your work, ideal for local feature development.\n\n**Workflow recommendation:**\n\n- Rebase freely on local feature branches\n- Clean up commits with interactive rebase before PR\n- Sync with main using rebase while branch is still private\n- Switch to merge once branch is shared/pushed\n- Use merge for final integration into main branch\n\nBy following these practices, you'll maintain clean git history without compromising team collaboration or risking lost work.\n\n---\n\n**Next Steps:**\n\n- Practice interactive rebase on a test repository\n- Set up `git config pull.rebase true` for cleaner pulls\n- Establish team conventions about when to merge vs rebase\n- Learn about `git reflog` for recovery options\n"}, {"name": "blog-post-vi.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Git Rebase vs Merge: L\u1ef1a Ch\u1ecdn \u0110\u00fang Cho Workflow C\u1ee7a B\u1ea1n\n\n> **D\u00e0nh cho developers mu\u1ed1n hi\u1ec3u s\u00e2u v\u1ec1 git history v\u00e0 collaboration best practices**\n\nB\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 bao gi\u1edd nh\u00ecn v\u00e0o git history c\u1ee7a project v\u00e0 th\u1ea5y n\u00f3 tr\u00f4ng nh\u01b0 m\u1ed9t m\u1edb h\u1ed7n \u0111\u1ed9n v\u1edbi v\u00f4 s\u1ed1 merge commits kh\u00f4ng? Ho\u1eb7c ng\u01b0\u1ee3c l\u1ea1i, b\u1ea1n t\u1eebng v\u00f4 t\u00ecnh rebase m\u1ed9t branch \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c push l\u00ean remote v\u00e0 l\u00e0m to\u00e0n team lo\u1ea1n l\u00ean? Vi\u1ec7c ch\u1ecdn gi\u1eefa `git merge` v\u00e0 `git rebase` l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng quy\u1ebft \u0111\u1ecbnh quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t \u1ea3nh h\u01b0\u1edfng \u0111\u1ebfn code collaboration.\n\nTrong b\u00e0i vi\u1ebft n\u00e0y, ch\u00fang ta s\u1ebd \u0111i s\u00e2u v\u00e0o c\u00e1ch ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng c\u1ee7a merge v\u00e0 rebase, khi n\u00e0o n\u00ean d\u00f9ng c\u00e1i n\u00e0o, v\u00e0 nh\u1eefng best practices \u0111\u1ec3 tr\u00e1nh g\u1eb7p r\u1eafc r\u1ed1i.\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 1: Hi\u1ec3u V\u1ec1 Git Merge\n\n### 1.1 Merge Ho\u1ea1t \u0110\u1ed9ng Nh\u01b0 Th\u1ebf N\u00e0o?\n\nGit merge t\u1ea1o ra m\u1ed9t **merge commit** m\u1edbi \u0111\u1ec3 k\u1ebft h\u1ee3p hai branches l\u1ea1i v\u1edbi nhau. Merge commit n\u00e0y c\u00f3 hai parent commits - m\u1ed9t t\u1eeb branch hi\u1ec7n t\u1ea1i v\u00e0 m\u1ed9t t\u1eeb branch \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c merge v\u00e0o.\n\n```bash\n# Merge feature branch v\u00e0o main\ngit checkout main\ngit merge feature-branch\n```\n\n**K\u1ebft qu\u1ea3 trong git history:**\n\n```\n A---B---C feature-branch\n / \\\nD---E---F---G---M main\n```\n\nCommit `M` l\u00e0 merge commit, n\u00f3 k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i history c\u1ee7a c\u1ea3 hai branches.\n\n### 1.2 \u01afu \u0110i\u1ec3m C\u1ee7a Merge\n\n**B\u1ea3o to\u00e0n to\u00e0n b\u1ed9 l\u1ecbch s\u1eed:**\n\n- M\u1ecdi commit \u0111\u1ec1u \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c gi\u1eef nguy\u00ean\n- Context \u0111\u1ea7y \u0111\u1ee7 v\u1ec1 khi n\u00e0o v\u00e0 nh\u01b0 th\u1ebf n\u00e0o c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c t\u00edch h\u1ee3p\n- D\u1ec5 d\u00e0ng truy v\u1ebft l\u1ea1i qu\u00e1 tr\u00ecnh ph\u00e1t tri\u1ec3n\n\n**An to\u00e0n cho team collaboration:**\n\n- Kh\u00f4ng thay \u0111\u1ed5i existing commits\n- Kh\u00f4ng conflict v\u1edbi nh\u1eefng g\u00ec \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c push l\u00ean remote\n- Transparent - m\u1ecdi ng\u01b0\u1eddi \u0111\u1ec1u th\u1ea5y \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c merge points\n\n```bash\n# Safe workflow cho team\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit merge main # Sync v\u1edbi latest main\ngit push origin feature-branch\n```\n\n### 1.3 Nh\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0110i\u1ec3m C\u1ee7a Merge\n\n**History c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 tr\u1edf n\u00ean r\u1ed1i:**\n\n```\n* Merge branch 'feature-1' into main\n|\\\n| * Fix typo\n| * Add tests\n| * Implement feature\n* | Merge branch 'feature-2' into main\n|\\|\n| * Another fix\n| * Some work\n* | Merge branch 'hotfix' into main\n```\n\nV\u1edbi nhi\u1ec1u features \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c develop song song, git history c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 tr\u1edf n\u00ean kh\u00f3 \u0111\u1ecdc v\u00e0 kh\u00f3 hi\u1ec3u lu\u1ed3ng ph\u00e1t tri\u1ec3n ch\u00ednh.\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 2: Hi\u1ec3u V\u1ec1 Git Rebase\n\n### 2.1 Rebase Ho\u1ea1t \u0110\u1ed9ng Nh\u01b0 Th\u1ebf N\u00e0o?\n\nGit rebase **vi\u1ebft l\u1ea1i history** b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch \u00e1p d\u1ee5ng l\u1ea1i c\u00e1c commits c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n l\u00ean tr\u00ean m\u1ed9t base commit m\u1edbi. Thay v\u00ec t\u1ea1o merge commit, rebase di chuy\u1ec3n to\u00e0n b\u1ed9 feature branch c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n \u0111\u1ebfn tip c\u1ee7a target branch.\n\n```bash\n# Rebase feature branch l\u00ean main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit rebase main\n```\n\n**Tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi rebase:**\n\n```\n A---B---C feature-branch\n /\nD---E---F---G main\n```\n\n**Sau khi rebase:**\n\n```\n A'---B'---C' feature-branch\n /\nD---E---F---G main\n```\n\nL\u01b0u \u00fd: `A'`, `B'`, `C'` l\u00e0 c\u00e1c commits **m\u1edbi** v\u1edbi SHA kh\u00e1c, m\u1eb7c d\u00f9 n\u1ed9i dung gi\u1ed1ng v\u1edbi `A`, `B`, `C`.\n\n### 2.2 \u01afu \u0110i\u1ec3m C\u1ee7a Rebase\n\n**Linear history - s\u1ea1ch \u0111\u1eb9p v\u00e0 d\u1ec5 \u0111\u1ecdc:**\n\n```bash\n# Linear history after rebase\nD---E---F---G---A---B---C\n```\n\nKh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 merge commits, m\u1ecdi th\u1ee9 theo m\u1ed9t \u0111\u01b0\u1eddng th\u1eb3ng. Khi \u0111\u1ecdc git log, b\u1ea1n th\u1ea5y ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c tr\u00ecnh t\u1ef1 c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c implement.\n\n**Git log r\u1ea5t clean:**\n\n```bash\n$ git log --oneline\nc3d2a1f (HEAD -> feature-branch) Add comprehensive tests\nb8e9f0c Implement user authentication\na7d6c5b Update dependencies\nf9e8d7c Merge pull request #42\n```\n\nSo v\u1edbi log c\u00f3 nhi\u1ec1u merge commits, linear history gi\u00fap easier \u0111\u1ec3 understand project evolution.\n\n### 2.3 Interactive Rebase - C\u00f4ng C\u1ee5 M\u1ea1nh M\u1ebd\n\nM\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng t\u00ednh n\u0103ng m\u1ea1nh nh\u1ea5t c\u1ee7a rebase l\u00e0 **interactive mode**:\n\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3\n```\n\n\u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y m\u1edf m\u1ed9t editor cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n:\n\n```\npick a7d6c5b Implement feature\npick b8e9f0c Fix bug\npick c3d2a1f Add tests\n\n# Commands:\n# p, pick = use commit\n# r, reword = use commit, but edit message\n# e, edit = use commit, but stop for amending\n# s, squash = meld into previous commit\n# f, fixup = like squash, but discard message\n# d, drop = remove commit\n```\n\n**Use cases ph\u1ed5 bi\u1ebfn:**\n\n**1. Squash commits tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi PR:**\n\n```bash\n# Thay v\u00ec:\n- WIP: initial work\n- Fix typo\n- Fix another typo\n- Actually fix the thing\n- Add tests\n\n# Th\u00e0nh:\n- Implement user authentication with tests\n```\n\n**2. Reorder commits logic:**\n\n```bash\n# S\u1eafp x\u1ebfp l\u1ea1i commits theo logic:\n- Add database migration\n- Update models\n- Add API endpoints\n- Add tests\n```\n\n**3. Clean up commit messages:**\n\n```bash\n# From: \"fixed stuff\" \"ugh why\" \"this works now\"\n# To: \"Refactor authentication flow\"\n \"Add comprehensive error handling\"\n \"Improve test coverage\"\n```\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 3: Khi N\u00e0o D\u00f9ng Merge, Khi N\u00e0o D\u00f9ng Rebase?\n\n### 3.1 The Golden Rule of Rebase\n\n> **KH\u00d4NG BAO GI\u1edc REBASE PUBLIC BRANCHES**\n\n\u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 rule quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t. N\u1ebfu branch c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c push l\u00ean remote v\u00e0 ng\u01b0\u1eddi kh\u00e1c c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 \u0111ang work tr\u00ean \u0111\u00f3, **\u0111\u1eebng rebase**.\n\n**T\u1ea1i sao?** V\u00ec rebase t\u1ea1o ra new commits v\u1edbi new SHAs. N\u1ebfu ai \u0111\u00f3 \u0111\u00e3 pull branch c\u0169, history c\u1ee7a h\u1ecd s\u1ebd conflict v\u1edbi rebased version:\n\n```\nYour teammate's local: Your rebased version:\nA---B---C A'---B'---C'\n\n# Git s\u1ebd th\u1ea5y \u0111\u00e2y nh\u01b0 diverged branches!\n```\n\nK\u1ebft qu\u1ea3: conflicts, confusion, v\u00e0 c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 m\u1ea5t code.\n\n### 3.2 Merge - An To\u00e0n Cho Shared Branches\n\n**D\u00f9ng MERGE khi:**\n\n\u2705 Integrating shared branches (main \u2190 feature)\n\u2705 Branch \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c publish/pushed ra remote\n\u2705 L\u00e0m vi\u1ec7c trong m\u1ed9t team (multiple people on same branch)\n\u2705 C\u1ea7n preserve \u0111\u1ea7y \u0111\u1ee7 context v\u00e0 history\n\u2705 Uncertainty v\u1ec1 ai \u0111ang work tr\u00ean branch\n\n**Workflow \u0111i\u1ec3n h\u00ecnh:**\n\n```bash\n# Feature development complete\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main\ngit merge feature-branch\ngit push origin main\n```\n\n### 3.3 Rebase - T\u1ed1t Cho Local Feature Branches\n\n**D\u00f9ng REBASE khi:**\n\n\u2705 Cleaning up local commits tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi PR\n\u2705 Branch c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n ch\u01b0a \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c share v\u1edbi ai\n\u2705 Mu\u1ed1n linear history\n\u2705 Sync feature branch v\u1edbi latest main\n\u2705 Feature branch development (before pushing)\n\n**Workflow \u0111i\u1ec3n h\u00ecnh:**\n\n```bash\n# Keep feature branch updated with main\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# Clean up commits before PR\ngit rebase -i HEAD~5\n\n# Now push (first time or with --force-with-lease)\ngit push origin feature-branch --force-with-lease\n```\n\n### 3.4 Git Pull Rebase - Best Practice\n\nKhi pull changes t\u1eeb remote, b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 hai options:\n\n```bash\n# Default: merge (creates merge commit)\ngit pull origin main\n\n# Rebase: linear history\ngit pull --rebase origin main\n# Ho\u1eb7c\ngit config pull.rebase true # Set as default\n```\n\n**Git pull --rebase workflow:**\n\n```\n# Before pull:\n Your local work\n D---E (local main)\n /\nA---B---C (remote main)\n\n# After git pull --rebase:\nA---B---C---D'---E' (main)\n```\n\n\u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y gi\u1eef history linear v\u00e0 tr\u00e1nh unnecessary merge commits t\u1eeb vi\u1ec7c sync v\u1edbi remote.\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 4: Best Practices v\u00e0 Common Pitfalls\n\n### 4.1 Feature Branch Workflow\n\n**Recommended approach:**\n\n```bash\n# 1. Start feature branch from main\ngit checkout -b feature/user-auth main\n\n# 2. Make commits as you work\ngit commit -m \"Add login endpoint\"\ngit commit -m \"Add password hashing\"\ngit commit -m \"Add tests\"\n\n# 3. Periodically sync with main (rebase while still private)\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# 4. Clean up commits before PR\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3 # Squash/reorganize\n\n# 5. Push to remote\ngit push origin feature/user-auth\n\n# 6. Create PR - t\u1eeb \u0111\u00e2y d\u00f9ng MERGE\n# After PR approved:\ngit checkout main\ngit pull origin main # Should include your merged PR\n```\n\n### 4.2 Safety v\u1edbi --force-with-lease\n\nN\u1ebfu b\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 rebase m\u1ed9t branch \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c push, b\u1ea1n c\u1ea7n force push. **Never use `--force`**, lu\u00f4n d\u00f9ng `--force-with-lease`:\n\n```bash\n# \u274c DANGEROUS\ngit push --force\n\n# \u2705 SAFER\ngit push --force-with-lease origin feature-branch\n```\n\n`--force-with-lease` ch\u1ec9 force push n\u1ebfu remote branch hasn't been updated since you last fetched. \u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y protect against accidentally overwriting work t\u1eeb teammates.\n\n### 4.3 Recovery From Rebase Mistakes\n\nN\u1ebfu rebase goes wrong, **\u0111\u1eebng panic**:\n\n```bash\n# Git gi\u1eef reference log c\u1ee7a m\u1ecdi operations\ngit reflog\n\n# Output:\n# c3d2a1f HEAD@{0}: rebase finished\n# a7d6c5b HEAD@{1}: rebase: Add tests\n# f9e8d7c HEAD@{2}: checkout: moving from main to feature\n\n# Reset v\u1ec1 state tr\u01b0\u1edbc rebase\ngit reset --hard HEAD@{2}\n```\n\nGit reflog l\u00e0 safety net c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n - n\u00f3 tracks t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 changes \u0111\u1ebfn HEAD, cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n undo almost anything.\n\n### 4.4 So S\u00e1nh Nhanh\n\n| Ti\u00eau ch\u00ed | Merge | Rebase |\n| :--------------- | :------------------------------- | :------------------------------------ |\n| **History** | Preserves all commits v\u00e0 context | Linear, cleaner history |\n| **Safety** | Very safe, no history rewriting | Requires caution with public branches |\n| **Team work** | Ideal cho collaboration | Good for solo feature work |\n| **Traceability** | Full context v\u1edbi merge points | Context c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 b\u1ecb lost |\n| **Complexity** | Simpler, straightforward | More powerful, requires understanding |\n| **Use case** | Integrating shared branches | Cleaning up local work |\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 5: Khi N\u00e0o C\u1ea3 Hai \u0110\u1ec1u OK?\n\nTrong practice, b\u1ea1n th\u01b0\u1eddng **combine both approaches**:\n\n```bash\n# Typical workflow combining both:\n\n# 1. Local feature development - s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng rebase t\u1ef1 do\ngit rebase -i HEAD~3 # Clean up commits\ngit rebase main # Stay updated with main\n\n# 2. Before creating PR\ngit push origin feature-branch\n\n# 3. Team review v\u00e0 updates tr\u00ean PR\n# Other developers c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 add commits\ngit pull origin feature-branch # Now d\u00f9ng merge!\n\n# 4. Final integration v\u00e0o main\n# Via PR merge (GitHub/GitLab handles this)\n# Most teams d\u00f9ng \"Squash and merge\" ho\u1eb7c \"Rebase and merge\"\n```\n\n## Key Takeaways\n\n\u2705 **Merge creates merge commits** - safe, preserves history, t\u1ed1t cho team collaboration\n\n\u2705 **Rebase rewrites history** - creates linear history, cleaner log, t\u1ed1t cho feature branches\n\n\u274c **Never rebase public/shared branches** - s\u1ebd cause conflicts v\u00e0 confusion\n\n\u2705 **Rebase local feature branches** tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi push or create PR - clean commit history\n\n\u2705 **Interactive rebase (`-i`)** l\u00e0 tool m\u1ea1nh m\u1ebd \u0111\u1ec3 clean up commits, reorder, squash\n\n\u2705 **Use `git pull --rebase`** \u0111\u1ec3 avoid unnecessary merge commits\n\n\u2705 **`--force-with-lease`** safer than `--force` khi c\u1ea7n force push\n\n\u2705 **Merge for integration**, **rebase for refinement**\n\n## K\u1ebft Lu\u1eadn\n\nChoosing gi\u1eefa merge v\u00e0 rebase kh\u00f4ng ph\u1ea3i l\u00e0 either/or decision - \u0111\u00f3 l\u00e0 about understanding **when to use each approach**. Merge provides safety v\u00e0 full context, perfect cho team collaboration v\u00e0 shared branches. Rebase gives you clean, linear history v\u00e0 powerful tools \u0111\u1ec3 refine your work, ideal cho local feature development.\n\n**Workflow recommendation:**\n\n- Rebase freely tr\u00ean local feature branches\n- Clean up commits v\u1edbi interactive rebase tr\u01b0\u1edbc PR\n- Sync v\u1edbi main using rebase while branch still private\n- Switch to merge once branch is shared/pushed\n- Use merge for final integration v\u00e0o main branch\n\nB\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch follow these practices, b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd maintain clean git history without compromising team collaboration hay risking lost work.\n\n---\n\n**Next Steps:**\n\n- Practice interactive rebase tr\u00ean a test repository\n- Set up `git config pull.rebase true` for cleaner pulls\n- Establish team conventions v\u1ec1 when to merge vs rebase\n- Learn about `git reflog` for recovery options\n"}], "grading": null}, {"id": "git-rebase-merge-without_skill", "prompt": "Transform casual notes about git rebase vs merge into professional blog post", "eval_id": 6, "outputs": [{"name": "git-rebase-vs-merge_en.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Git Rebase vs Merge: Choosing the Right Strategy for Your Workflow\n\nWhen working with Git, one of the most common dilemmas developers face is deciding between `git rebase` and `git merge`. Both commands integrate changes from one branch into another, but they do so in fundamentally different ways. Understanding these differences is crucial for maintaining a clean, manageable codebase.\n\n## The Fundamental Difference\n\n### Git Merge: The Safe Choice\n\nWhen you run `git merge`, Git creates a new **merge commit** that ties together the histories of two branches. This commit has two parent commits, preserving the complete history of both branches exactly as they happened.\n\n```bash\ngit checkout main\ngit merge feature-branch\n```\n\nThis approach maintains the entire context of when and how changes were integrated, making it easy to see the full story of your project's development.\n\n### Git Rebase: The History Rewriter\n\nIn contrast, `git rebase` **rewrites history**. It takes your commits from one branch and replays them on top of another branch, creating entirely new commits with different SHA hashes.\n\n```bash\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit rebase main\n```\n\nThe result? A **linear history** that looks like all your work happened sequentially, one commit after another, with no branching and merging complexity.\n\n## Why Choose Rebase? The Case for Clean History\n\nRebase creates a beautifully linear commit history that's easier to read and understand. When you look at your project's history, it tells a clean story without the noise of countless merge commits cluttering the timeline.\n\nThis linear approach makes it simpler to:\n\n- Follow the logical progression of changes\n- Use tools like `git bisect` to find bugs\n- Review the project history without getting lost in merge commit webs\n\n## The Golden Rule: Never Rebase Public Branches\n\nHere's where things get serious: **never rebase branches that have been pushed to a shared repository and that others are working on**. Why? Because rebase rewrites history by creating new commits with different SHA hashes.\n\nIf you rebase a public branch:\n\n1. Your commits get new SHA hashes\n2. Other developers' local branches point to the old commits\n3. Chaos ensues when they try to push or pull\n4. Hours (or days) of frustration follow\n\n**Merge is safer for teams** precisely because it doesn't rewrite history. It simply adds new commits on top of existing ones, so everyone's local repositories stay in sync.\n\n## The Best of Both Worlds: Strategic Rebase Usage\n\nThe sweet spot? **Use rebase for your local feature branches before creating a PR**.\n\nHere's a typical workflow:\n\n```bash\n# Working on your feature branch\ngit checkout feature-branch\n\n# Before submitting PR, rebase on latest main\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# Now your changes sit cleanly on top of main\n```\n\nThis gives you the cleaner history of rebase while keeping shared branches safe with merge.\n\n## Interactive Rebase: Your Commit Cleanup Tool\n\nOne of rebase's superpowers is **interactive rebase** (`git rebase -i`), which lets you clean up your commits before sharing them:\n\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~5\n```\n\nThis opens an editor where you can:\n\n- **Reword** commit messages\n- **Squash** multiple commits into one\n- **Reorder** commits\n- **Drop** commits entirely\n- **Edit** commit content\n\nIt's perfect for turning your messy, work-in-progress commits into a polished, logical series of changes.\n\n## Git Pull --rebase: A Daily Time-Saver\n\nInstead of `git pull` (which does a fetch + merge), use:\n\n```bash\ngit pull --rebase\n```\n\nThis fetches remote changes and rebases your local commits on top of them, avoiding unnecessary merge commits for simple updates. It keeps your local branch history cleaner without the risks of rebasing public branches.\n\nYou can even make it your default:\n\n```bash\ngit config --global pull.rebase true\n```\n\n## Decision Matrix: When to Use Each\n\n| Scenario | Use Merge | Use Rebase |\n| ---------------------------------------- | --------- | ------------------ |\n| Integrating a feature into main | \u2705 | \u274c |\n| Updating feature branch with latest main | \u2705 | \u2705 (if not pushed) |\n| Cleaning up commits before PR | \u274c | \u2705 |\n| Working on a public/shared branch | \u2705 | \u274c |\n| Pulling latest changes | \u2705 | \u2705 (via --rebase) |\n| Multiple people on same feature branch | \u2705 | \u274c |\n\n## Final Thoughts\n\nBoth merge and rebase are powerful tools, and the best Git users know when to use each:\n\n- **Merge** preserves history and is safer for collaboration\n- **Rebase** creates cleaner history but requires care and discipline\n\nThe key is to use rebase **locally and privately** to polish your work, then use merge to integrate those polished changes into shared branches. Follow this approach, and you'll maintain both a clean commit history and a happy team.\n\nRemember: with great rebase power comes great responsibility. When in doubt, merge. Your teammates will thank you.\n\n---\n\n_Have questions about Git workflows? C\u1ea3 hai l\u1ec7nh \u0111\u1ec1u t\u00edch h\u1ee3p thay \u0111\u1ed5i t\u1eeb branch n\u00e0y sang branch kh\u00e1c, nh\u01b0ng ch\u00fang th\u1ef1c hi\u1ec7n theo nh\u1eefng c\u00e1ch ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n kh\u00e1c nhau. Hi\u1ec3u r\u00f5 nh\u1eefng \u0111i\u1ec3m kh\u00e1c bi\u1ec7t n\u00e0y l\u00e0 r\u1ea5t quan tr\u1ecdng \u0111\u1ec3 duy tr\u00ec m\u1ed9t codebase s\u1ea1ch v\u00e0 d\u1ec5 qu\u1ea3n l\u00fd.\n\n## S\u1ef1 Kh\u00e1c Bi\u1ec7t C\u01a1 B\u1ea3n\n\n### Git Merge: L\u1ef1a Ch\u1ecdn An To\u00e0n\n\nKhi b\u1ea1n ch\u1ea1y `git merge`, Git t\u1ea1o ra m\u1ed9t **merge commit** m\u1edbi \u0111\u1ec3 k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i l\u1ecbch s\u1eed c\u1ee7a hai branch l\u1ea1i v\u1edbi nhau. Commit n\u00e0y c\u00f3 hai parent commits, gi\u1eef nguy\u00ean ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n l\u1ecbch s\u1eed c\u1ee7a c\u1ea3 hai branch \u0111\u00fang nh\u01b0 c\u00e1ch ch\u00fang \u0111\u00e3 x\u1ea3y ra.\n\n```bash\ngit checkout main\ngit merge feature-branch\n```\n\nC\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn n\u00e0y duy tr\u00ec to\u00e0n b\u1ed9 context v\u1ec1 th\u1eddi \u0111i\u1ec3m v\u00e0 c\u00e1ch th\u1ee9c c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c t\u00edch h\u1ee3p, gi\u00fap d\u1ec5 d\u00e0ng nh\u00ecn th\u1ea5y c\u00e2u chuy\u1ec7n \u0111\u1ea7y \u0111\u1ee7 v\u1ec1 s\u1ef1 ph\u00e1t tri\u1ec3n c\u1ee7a d\u1ef1 \u00e1n.\n\n### Git Rebase: Ng\u01b0\u1eddi Vi\u1ebft L\u1ea1i L\u1ecbch S\u1eed\n\nNg\u01b0\u1ee3c l\u1ea1i, `git rebase` **vi\u1ebft l\u1ea1i l\u1ecbch s\u1eed**. N\u00f3 l\u1ea5y c\u00e1c commits c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n t\u1eeb m\u1ed9t branch v\u00e0 replay ch\u00fang l\u00ean tr\u00ean m\u1ed9t branch kh\u00e1c, t\u1ea1o ra c\u00e1c commits ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n m\u1edbi v\u1edbi SHA hashes kh\u00e1c nhau.\n\n```bash\ngit checkout feature-branch\ngit rebase main\n```\n\nK\u1ebft qu\u1ea3? M\u1ed9t **l\u1ecbch s\u1eed tuy\u1ebfn t\u00ednh** tr\u00f4ng gi\u1ed1ng nh\u01b0 t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 c\u00f4ng vi\u1ec7c c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 di\u1ec5n ra tu\u1ea7n t\u1ef1, commit n\u00e0y sau commit kia, kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 s\u1ef1 ph\u1ee9c t\u1ea1p c\u1ee7a vi\u1ec7c ph\u00e2n nh\u00e1nh v\u00e0 merge.\n\n## T\u1ea1i Sao Ch\u1ecdn Rebase? L\u00fd Do Cho L\u1ecbch S\u1eed S\u1ea1ch \u0110\u1eb9p\n\nRebase t\u1ea1o ra m\u1ed9t l\u1ecbch s\u1eed commit tuy\u1ebfn t\u00ednh \u0111\u1eb9p m\u1eaft, d\u1ec5 \u0111\u1ecdc v\u00e0 d\u1ec5 hi\u1ec3u h\u01a1n. Khi b\u1ea1n nh\u00ecn v\u00e0o l\u1ecbch s\u1eed d\u1ef1 \u00e1n, n\u00f3 k\u1ec3 m\u1ed9t c\u00e2u chuy\u1ec7n m\u1ea1ch l\u1ea1c m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 ti\u1ebfng \u1ed3n t\u1eeb v\u00f4 s\u1ed1 merge commits l\u00e0m l\u1ed9n x\u1ed9n timeline.\n\nC\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn tuy\u1ebfn t\u00ednh n\u00e0y gi\u00fap \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n h\u00f3a vi\u1ec7c:\n\n- Theo d\u00f5i ti\u1ebfn tr\u00ecnh logic c\u1ee7a c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i\n- S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng c\u00e1c c\u00f4ng c\u1ee5 nh\u01b0 `git bisect` \u0111\u1ec3 t\u00ecm bugs\n- Review l\u1ecbch s\u1eed d\u1ef1 \u00e1n m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng b\u1ecb l\u1ea1c trong m\u1ea1ng l\u01b0\u1edbi merge commits\n\n## Quy T\u1eafc V\u00e0ng: Kh\u00f4ng Bao Gi\u1edd Rebase Public Branches\n\n\u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 \u0111i\u1ec1u nghi\u00eam t\u00fac: **kh\u00f4ng bao gi\u1edd rebase c\u00e1c branch \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c push l\u00ean shared repository m\u00e0 ng\u01b0\u1eddi kh\u00e1c \u0111ang l\u00e0m vi\u1ec7c**. T\u1ea1i sao? B\u1edfi v\u00ec rebase vi\u1ebft l\u1ea1i l\u1ecbch s\u1eed b\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch t\u1ea1o c\u00e1c commits m\u1edbi v\u1edbi SHA hashes kh\u00e1c nhau.\n\nN\u1ebfu b\u1ea1n rebase m\u1ed9t public branch:\n\n1. C\u00e1c commits c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n nh\u1eadn SHA hashes m\u1edbi\n2. Local branches c\u1ee7a developers kh\u00e1c v\u1eabn tr\u1ecf \u0111\u1ebfn c\u00e1c commits c\u0169\n3. H\u1ed7n lo\u1ea1n x\u1ea3y ra khi h\u1ecd c\u1ed1 g\u1eafng push ho\u1eb7c pull\n4. H\u00e0ng gi\u1edd (ho\u1eb7c h\u00e0ng ng\u00e0y) frustration theo sau\n\n**Merge an to\u00e0n h\u01a1n cho teams** ch\u00ednh x\u00e1c v\u00ec n\u00f3 kh\u00f4ng vi\u1ebft l\u1ea1i l\u1ecbch s\u1eed. N\u00f3 ch\u1ec9 \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n th\u00eam commits m\u1edbi l\u00ean tr\u00ean c\u00e1c commits hi\u1ec7n c\u00f3, v\u00ec v\u1eady local repositories c\u1ee7a m\u1ecdi ng\u01b0\u1eddi \u0111\u1ec1u gi\u1eef \u0111\u1ed3ng b\u1ed9.\n\n## T\u1eadn D\u1ee5ng \u01afu \u0110i\u1ec3m C\u1ee7a C\u1ea3 Hai: S\u1eed D\u1ee5ng Rebase Chi\u1ebfn L\u01b0\u1ee3c\n\n\u0110i\u1ec3m t\u1ed1i \u01b0u? **S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng rebase cho local feature branches c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi t\u1ea1o PR**.\n\n\u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 m\u1ed9t quy tr\u00ecnh \u0111i\u1ec3n h\u00ecnh:\n\n```bash\n# \u0110ang l\u00e0m vi\u1ec7c tr\u00ean feature branch\ngit checkout feature-branch\n\n# Tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi submit PR, rebase l\u00ean main m\u1edbi nh\u1ea5t\ngit fetch origin\ngit rebase origin/main\n\n# B\u00e2y gi\u1edd c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n n\u1eb1m g\u1ecdn g\u00e0ng tr\u00ean top c\u1ee7a main\n```\n\n\u0110i\u1ec1u n\u00e0y mang l\u1ea1i cho b\u1ea1n l\u1ecbch s\u1eed s\u1ea1ch h\u01a1n c\u1ee7a rebase trong khi v\u1eabn gi\u1eef c\u00e1c shared branches an to\u00e0n v\u1edbi merge.\n\n## Interactive Rebase: C\u00f4ng C\u1ee5 D\u1ecdn D\u1eb9p Commits\n\nM\u1ed9t trong nh\u1eefng si\u00eau n\u0103ng l\u1ef1c c\u1ee7a rebase l\u00e0 **interactive rebase** (`git rebase -i`), cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n d\u1ecdn d\u1eb9p commits tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi share ch\u00fang:\n\n```bash\ngit rebase -i HEAD~5\n```\n\nL\u1ec7nh n\u00e0y m\u1edf m\u1ed9t editor n\u01a1i b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 th\u1ec3:\n\n- **Reword** commit messages\n- **Squash** nhi\u1ec1u commits th\u00e0nh m\u1ed9t\n- **Reorder** commits\n- **Drop** commits ho\u00e0n to\u00e0n\n- **Edit** n\u1ed9i dung commit\n\nN\u00f3 ho\u00e0n h\u1ea3o \u0111\u1ec3 bi\u1ebfn c\u00e1c commits l\u1ed9n x\u1ed9n, work-in-progress c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n th\u00e0nh m\u1ed9t chu\u1ed7i thay \u0111\u1ed5i b\u00f3ng b\u1ea9y v\u00e0 logic.\n\n## Git Pull --rebase: Ti\u1ebft Ki\u1ec7m Th\u1eddi Gian H\u00e0ng Ng\u00e0y\n\nThay v\u00ec `git pull` (th\u1ef1c hi\u1ec7n fetch + merge), h\u00e3y s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng:\n\n```bash\ngit pull --rebase\n```\n\nL\u1ec7nh n\u00e0y fetch c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i t\u1eeb remote v\u00e0 rebase c\u00e1c local commits c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n l\u00ean tr\u00ean ch\u00fang, tr\u00e1nh c\u00e1c merge commits kh\u00f4ng c\u1ea7n thi\u1ebft cho c\u00e1c updates \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n. N\u00f3 gi\u1eef l\u1ecbch s\u1eed local branch c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n s\u1ea1ch h\u01a1n m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng g\u1eb7p r\u1ee7i ro c\u1ee7a vi\u1ec7c rebase public branches.\n\nB\u1ea1n th\u1eadm ch\u00ed c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 \u0111\u1eb7t n\u00f3 l\u00e0m m\u1eb7c \u0111\u1ecbnh:\n\n```bash\ngit config --global pull.rebase true\n```\n\n## Ma Tr\u1eadn Quy\u1ebft \u0110\u1ecbnh: Khi N\u00e0o S\u1eed D\u1ee5ng C\u00e1i G\u00ec\n\n| T\u00ecnh Hu\u1ed1ng | D\u00f9ng Merge | D\u00f9ng Rebase |\n| ----------------------------------------- | ---------- | ------------------ |\n| T\u00edch h\u1ee3p feature v\u00e0o main | \u2705 | \u274c |\n| C\u1eadp nh\u1eadt feature branch v\u1edbi main m\u1edbi nh\u1ea5t | \u2705 | \u2705 (n\u1ebfu ch\u01b0a push) |\n| D\u1ecdn d\u1eb9p commits tr\u01b0\u1edbc PR | \u274c | \u2705 |\n| L\u00e0m vi\u1ec7c tr\u00ean public/shared branch | \u2705 | \u274c |\n| Pull c\u00e1c thay \u0111\u1ed5i m\u1edbi nh\u1ea5t | \u2705 | \u2705 (qua --rebase) |\n| Nhi\u1ec1u ng\u01b0\u1eddi tr\u00ean c\u00f9ng feature branch | \u2705 | \u274c |\n\n## Suy Ngh\u0129 Cu\u1ed1i C\u00f9ng\n\nC\u1ea3 merge v\u00e0 rebase \u0111\u1ec1u l\u00e0 nh\u1eefng c\u00f4ng c\u1ee5 m\u1ea1nh m\u1ebd, v\u00e0 nh\u1eefng Git users gi\u1ecfi nh\u1ea5t bi\u1ebft khi n\u00e0o s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng m\u1ed7i c\u00e1i:\n\n- **Merge** b\u1ea3o to\u00e0n l\u1ecbch s\u1eed v\u00e0 an to\u00e0n h\u01a1n cho collaboration\n- **Rebase** t\u1ea1o l\u1ecbch s\u1eed s\u1ea1ch h\u01a1n nh\u01b0ng \u0111\u00f2i h\u1ecfi s\u1ef1 c\u1ea9n th\u1eadn v\u00e0 k\u1ef7 lu\u1eadt\n\nCh\u00eca kh\u00f3a l\u00e0 s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng rebase **locally v\u00e0 privately** \u0111\u1ec3 \u0111\u00e1nh b\u00f3ng c\u00f4ng vi\u1ec7c c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n, sau \u0111\u00f3 s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng merge \u0111\u1ec3 t\u00edch h\u1ee3p nh\u1eefng thay \u0111\u1ed5i \u0111\u00e3 \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c \u0111\u00e1nh b\u00f3ng \u0111\u00f3 v\u00e0o c\u00e1c shared branches. Theo c\u00e1ch ti\u1ebfp c\u1eadn n\u00e0y, v\u00e0 b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd duy tr\u00ec \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c c\u1ea3 l\u1ecbch s\u1eed commit s\u1ea1ch \u0111\u1eb9p l\u1eabn m\u1ed9t team vui v\u1ebb.\n\nH\u00e3y nh\u1edb: v\u1edbi s\u1ee9c m\u1ea1nh rebase to l\u1edbn \u0111i k\u00e8m tr\u00e1ch nhi\u1ec7m to l\u1edbn. Khi c\u00f2n nghi ng\u1edd, h\u00e3y merge. Teammates c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd c\u1ea3m \u01a1n b\u1ea1n.\n\n---\n\n_C\u00f3 c\u00e2u h\u1ecfi v\u1ec1 Git workflows? Or how Google Docs allows multiple people to edit the same document simultaneously? The answer lies in WebSocket technology - a protocol that enables bidirectional, real-time communication between client and server.\n\nIn this article, we'll explore WebSocket from the fundamental problems of traditional HTTP, how WebSocket solves those issues, and how to implement a simple chat application.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: The Problem with Traditional HTTP\n\n### 1.1 HTTP: The Request-Response Model\n\nHTTP (Hypertext Transfer Protocol) is the foundation of the Web, but it's designed around a **request-response model**:\n\n```\nClient Server\n | |\n |-------- Request -------->|\n | |\n |<------- Response --------|\n | |\n [Connection Closed]\n```\n\nEvery time the client needs new data:\n\n1. Open a new connection\n2. Send a request\n3. Receive a response\n4. Close the connection\n\n**The problem**: The client can't know when the server has new data. The server also can't proactively send data to the client.\n\n### 1.2 Temporary Workarounds\n\nTo address this limitation, developers have had to use techniques like:\n\n- **Polling**: Client continuously sends requests to check for new data\n - \u274c Wastes bandwidth\n - \u274c Increases server load\n - \u274c High latency (delay between requests)\n\n- **Long Polling**: Client sends a request and server holds the connection until new data is available\n - \u26a0\ufe0f More complex\n - \u26a0\ufe0f Still resource-intensive\n\nNone of these solutions are truly efficient for real-time applications.\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: WebSocket - The Real-Time Communication Solution\n\n### 2.1 What is WebSocket?\n\n**WebSocket** is a communication protocol that provides a **persistent connection** between client and server with bidirectional capabilities.\n\n| Feature | HTTP | WebSocket |\n| :------------- | :------------------------- | :------------------------- |\n| **Connection** | Closes after each request | Stays open continuously |\n| **Direction** | Request \u2192 Response | Bidirectional |\n| **Overhead** | Headers with every request | Minimal after handshake |\n| **Real-time** | No (requires polling) | Yes (true real-time) |\n| **Use Case** | APIs, web pages | Chat, gaming, live updates |\n\n### 2.2 How WebSocket Works\n\nWebSocket starts as an HTTP request, then \"upgrades\" to the WebSocket protocol:\n\n```\nClient Server\n | |\n |------ HTTP Upgrade Request ---->|\n | (Contains: Upgrade: websocket) |\n | |\n |<----- Switching Protocols ------|\n | (Status: 101) |\n | |\n |====== WebSocket Connection =====|\n | |\n |<-------- Message --------------->|\n |<-------- Message ----------------|\n |---------- Message -------------->|\n | |\n [Connection stays open]\n```\n\n**Detailed steps:**\n\n1. **Handshake**: Client sends HTTP request with `Upgrade: websocket` header\n2. **Upgrade**: Server responds with status `101 Switching Protocols`\n3. **Connection Open**: Connection is kept open\n4. **Bidirectional Communication**: Both sides can send messages at any time\n5. **Close**: Either side can close the connection when needed\n\n### 2.3 WebSocket Advantages\n\n**Real-Time Communication**\n\n- Data is sent immediately, no polling required\n- Low latency (< 100ms)\n\n**Efficient**\n\n- Connection is reused\n- No HTTP header overhead for each message\n- Significantly reduces server load\n\n**Bidirectional**\n\n- Server can push data to client at any time\n- Client can send data to server at any time\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Common Use Cases\n\n### 3.1 Chat Applications\n\nChat applications need:\n\n- Instant message delivery\n- Typing indicators\n- Online status updates\n\n**Examples**: Slack, Discord, Facebook Messenger\n\n### 3.2 Live Notifications\n\nReal-time notifications for:\n\n- Social media updates (likes, comments)\n- System alerts\n- User activity notifications\n\n**Examples**: Twitter notifications, GitHub notifications\n\n### 3.3 Collaborative Editing\n\nMultiple users editing the same document simultaneously:\n\n- See others' changes in real-time\n- Collaborator cursor positions\n- Conflict resolution\n\n**Examples**: Google Docs, Figma, CodeSandbox\n\n### 3.4 Gaming\n\nOnline multiplayer games need:\n\n- Player position updates\n- Game state synchronization\n- Low latency actions\n\n**Examples**: Agar.io, Slither.io, multiplayer browser games\n\n### 3.5 Stock Tickers and Financial Data\n\nFinancial applications need:\n\n- Live price updates\n- Trading activity\n- Market data streams\n\n**Examples**: Trading platforms, cryptocurrency exchanges\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Socket.io vs Native WebSocket\n\n### 4.1 Detailed Comparison\n\n| Feature | Native WebSocket | Socket.io |\n| :------------------------- | :------------------------- | :---------------------------- |\n| **Learning Curve** | Easy to learn | Moderate |\n| **Browser Support** | Modern browsers | Wide support (with fallbacks) |\n| **Automatic Reconnection** | \u274c Must implement yourself | \u2705 Built-in |\n| **Rooms & Namespaces** | \u274c Not available | \u2705 Built-in |\n| **Broadcasting** | \u274c Must code yourself | \u2705 Easy API |\n| **Fallback Options** | \u274c None | \u2705 Long polling, etc. |\n| **Bundle Size** | Very small (~0 KB) | ~50 KB (minified) |\n| **Performance** | Fastest | Good (slight overhead) |\n| **Best For** | Simple use cases, control | Complex apps, reliability |\n\n### 4.2 When to Use Native WebSocket\n\n**Choose Native WebSocket when:**\n\n- You need maximum performance\n- Simple application without complex features\n- Targeting modern browsers only\n- Want complete control over implementation\n- Bundle size matters\n\n**Code example:**\n\n```javascript\nconst ws = new WebSocket(\"ws://localhost:8080\");\n\nws.onopen = () => {\n console.log(\"Connected\");\n ws.send(\"Hello Server\");\n};\n\nws.onmessage = (event) => {\n console.log(\"Received:\", event.data);\n};\n```\n\n### 4.3 When to Use Socket.io\n\n**Choose Socket.io when:**\n\n- Need to support older browsers\n- Want automatic reconnection\n- Need rooms/namespaces for multi-tenancy\n- Want simple broadcasting\n- Need reliability and fallback mechanisms\n\n**Socket.io provides:**\n\n- Event-based API (emit/on)\n- Rooms to group clients\n- Namespaces to organize logic\n- Middleware support\n- Binary data support\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Building a Simple Chat with Socket.io\n\n### 5.1 Project Setup\n\n```bash\n# Install dependencies\nnpm init -y\nnpm install express socket.io\n```\n\n### 5.2 Server Code (server.js)\n\n```javascript\nconst express = require(\"express\");\nconst { createServer } = require(\"http\");\nconst { Server } = require(\"socket.io\");\n\nconst app = express();\nconst httpServer = createServer(app);\nconst io = new Server(httpServer);\n\n// Serve static files\napp.use(express.static(\"public\"));\n\n// Track online users\nlet onlineUsers = 0;\n\n// Socket.io connection handler\nio.on(\"connection\", (socket) => {\n onlineUsers++;\n console.log(`User connected. Online: ${onlineUsers}`);\n\n // Broadcast to all clients\n io.emit(\"user-count\", onlineUsers);\n\n // Listen for chat messages\n socket.on(\"chat-message\", (data) => {\n // Broadcast message to all clients\n io.emit(\"chat-message\", {\n username: data.username,\n message: data.message,\n timestamp: new Date().toISOString(),\n });\n });\n\n // Listen for typing events\n socket.on(\"typing\", (username) => {\n socket.broadcast.emit(\"typing\", username);\n });\n\n // Handle disconnect\n socket.on(\"disconnect\", () => {\n onlineUsers--;\n io.emit(\"user-count\", onlineUsers);\n console.log(`User disconnected. Online: ${onlineUsers}`);\n });\n});\n\n// Start server\nconst PORT = process.env.PORT || 3000;\nhttpServer.listen(PORT, () => {\n console.log(`Server running on http://localhost:${PORT}`);\n});\n```\n\n### 5.3 Client Code (public/index.html)\n\n```html\n\n\n \n \n \n WebSocket Chat\n \n \n \n
\n
\n

WebSocket Chat

\n
0 online
\n
\n\n
\n\n
\n\n
\n \n \n \n
\n
\n\n \n \n \n\n```\n\n### 5.4 Running the Application\n\n```bash\n# Start server\nnode server.js\n\n# Open in browser\n# http://localhost:3000\n\n# Open multiple tabs to test chat\n```\n\n**Features implemented:**\n\n- \u2705 Real-time messaging\n- \u2705 Online user count\n- \u2705 Typing indicators\n- \u2705 Timestamps\n- \u2705 Auto-scroll to latest message\n- \u2705 Enter key to send\n- \u2705 Responsive design\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\n### Key Takeaways\n\n1. **HTTP wasn't designed for real-time** \u2014 The request-response model isn't suitable for applications needing continuous updates.\n\n2. **WebSocket provides persistent, bidirectional connection** \u2014 Allows server to push data and client to send data at any time.\n\n3. **Socket.io vs Native WebSocket** \u2014 Socket.io is easier with more features, Native WebSocket is lighter and faster.\n\n4. **Use cases are diverse** \u2014 From chat, notifications, collaborative editing to gaming and financial data.\n\n### Next Steps\n\n**To learn more about WebSocket:**\n\n1. **Explore advanced Socket.io features**\n - Rooms and namespaces\n - Middleware and authentication\n - Binary data transmission\n\n2. **Learn about scaling**\n - Redis adapter for multiple server instances\n - Load balancing with sticky sessions\n - Horizontal scaling strategies\n\n3. **Security best practices**\n - Authentication and authorization\n - Rate limiting\n - Input validation and sanitization\n\n4. **Alternatives to explore**\n - Server-Sent Events (SSE) for one-way communication\n - WebRTC for peer-to-peer connections\n - GraphQL Subscriptions\n\n### Resources\n\n- [MDN WebSocket API](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WebSocket)\n- [Socket.io Documentation](https://socket.io/docs/v4/)\n- [WebSocket RFC 6455](https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6455)\n\n---\n\n**Happy coding!
