Rooms v\u00e0 namespaces\n - Middleware v\u00e0 authentication\n - Binary data transmission\n\n2. **Learn about scaling**\n - Redis adapter cho multiple server instances\n - Load balancing v\u1edbi sticky sessions\n - Horizontal scaling strategies\n\n3. **Security best practices**\n - Authentication v\u00e0 authorization\n - Rate limiting\n - Input validation v\u00e0 sanitization\n\n4. **Alternatives to explore**\n - Server-Sent Events (SSE) cho one-way communication\n - WebRTC cho peer-to-peer connections\n - GraphQL Subscriptions\n\n### Resources\n\n- [MDN WebSocket API](https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/API/WebSocket)\n- [Socket.io Documentation](https://socket.io/docs/v4/)\n- [WebSocket RFC 6455](https://datatracker.ietf.org/doc/html/rfc6455)\n\n---\n\n**Happy coding! \ud83d\ude80**\n"}], "grading": null}, {"id": "websockets-without_skill", "prompt": "Create blog post from notes about WebSockets", "eval_id": 7, "outputs": [{"name": "websockets-guide-english.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Understanding WebSockets: Real-Time Communication for Modern Web Apps\n\n## What Are WebSockets?\n\nWebSocket is a communication protocol that provides a **persistent connection** between a client and server, enabling real-time, bidirectional data exchange. Unlike traditional HTTP, which follows a request-response model and closes the connection after each interaction, WebSocket maintains an open channel where both the client and server can send messages to each other at any time.\n\n## WebSocket vs. HTTP: Key Differences\n\n| Feature | HTTP | WebSocket |\n| ------------- | ------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------- |\n| Connection | Request-response, closes after each request | Persistent, stays open |\n| Communication | Unidirectional (client requests, server responds) | Bidirectional (both can initiate) |\n| Real-time | Polling required for updates | Native real-time support |\n| Overhead | High (headers sent with each request) | Low (after initial handshake) |\n\n## Real-World Use Cases\n\nWebSockets shine in applications that require instant, two-way communication:\n\n### 1. **Chat Applications**\n\nReal-time messaging where users send and receive messages instantly without page refreshes.\n\n### 2. **Live Notifications**\n\nPush notifications that appear immediately when events occur on the server.\n\n### 3. **Collaborative Editing**\n\nGoogle Docs-style applications where multiple users edit simultaneously and see each other's changes in real-time.\n\n### 4. **Gaming**\n\nMultiplayer games requiring low-latency communication between players and game servers.\n\n### 5. **Stock Tickers & Live Dashboards**\n\nFinancial applications displaying real-time price updates and market data.\n\n## How WebSockets Work\n\nThe WebSocket lifecycle involves three main phases:\n\n### 1. **HTTP Handshake**\n\nThe connection starts as a standard HTTP request with special headers indicating the client wants to upgrade to WebSocket:\n\n```\nGET /chat HTTP/1.1\nHost: example.com\nUpgrade: websocket\nConnection: Upgrade\n```\n\n### 2. **Protocol Upgrade**\n\nIf the server supports WebSocket, it responds with a 101 status code, upgrading the connection from HTTP to the WebSocket protocol.\n\n### 3. **Open Connection**\n\nOnce upgraded, the connection stays open, and both client and server can send messages to each other at any time without the overhead of HTTP headers.\n\n## Socket.io vs. Native WebSocket\n\nWhen implementing WebSocket in your application, you have two main options:\n\n### Socket.io\n\n**Advantages:**\n\n- Easier to use with a simpler API\n- Automatic fallbacks to long-polling if WebSocket isn't available\n- Built-in support for rooms and namespaces\n- Automatic reconnection handling\n- Broadcasting capabilities\n\n**When to use:** Most web applications, especially when you need reliability across different browsers and network conditions.\n\n### Native WebSocket\n\n**Advantages:**\n\n- More control over the implementation\n- Lighter weight (no additional library)\n- Lower overhead\n- Standard browser API\n\n**When to use:** Performance-critical applications where you need full control and can handle edge cases manually.\n\n## Quick Start: Building a Simple Chat with Socket.io\n\nHere's a minimal example of a real-time chat application using Socket.io:\n\n### Server (Node.js)\n\n```javascript\nconst express = require(\"express\");\nconst http = require(\"http\");\nconst socketIO = require(\"socket.io\");\n\nconst app = express();\nconst server = http.createServer(app);\nconst io = socketIO(server);\n\napp.use(express.static(\"public\"));\n\n// Handle socket connections\nio.on(\"connection\", (socket) => {\n console.log(\"New user connected\");\n\n // Listen for chat messages\n socket.on(\"chat message\", (msg) => {\n // Broadcast message to all connected clients\n io.emit(\"chat message\", msg);\n });\n\n // Handle disconnection\n socket.on(\"disconnect\", () => {\n console.log(\"User disconnected\");\n });\n});\n\nconst PORT = process.env.PORT || 3000;\nserver.listen(PORT, () => {\n console.log(`Server running on port ${PORT}`);\n});\n```\n\n### Client (HTML + JavaScript)\n\n```html\n\n\n \n Simple Chat\n \n \n \n

Simple Chat Room

\n
    \n
    \n \n \n \n\n \n \n \n\n```\n\n### Installation\n\n```bash\nnpm init -y\nnpm install express socket.io\nnode server.js\n```\n\nVisit `http://localhost:3000` in multiple browser tabs to test the chat!\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **Handle Reconnection**: Always implement reconnection logic for dropped connections\n2. **Validate Messages**: Sanitize and validate all incoming messages on the server\n3. **Use Rooms**: Organize users into logical groups using Socket.io rooms\n4. **Monitor Performance**: Keep an eye on the number of open connections\n5. **Implement Authentication**: Secure your WebSocket connections with proper auth\n\n## Conclusion\n\nWebSockets provide a powerful way to build real-time, interactive web applications. Whether you choose Socket.io for its convenience or native WebSocket for performance, understanding this technology opens up possibilities for creating engaging user experiences with instant updates and seamless collaboration.\n\nStart small with a simple chat or notification system, and you'll quickly see how WebSockets can transform your applications!\n\n---\n\n_Published: March 17, 2026_\n"}, {"name": "websockets-guide-vietnamese.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Hi\u1ec3u v\u1ec1 WebSocket: Giao ti\u1ebfp Real-Time cho \u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng Web Hi\u1ec7n \u0111\u1ea1i\n\n## WebSocket l\u00e0 g\u00ec?\n\nWebSocket l\u00e0 giao th\u1ee9c truy\u1ec1n th\u00f4ng cung c\u1ea5p **k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i li\u00ean t\u1ee5c** gi\u1eefa client v\u00e0 server, cho ph\u00e9p trao \u0111\u1ed5i d\u1eef li\u1ec7u hai chi\u1ec1u theo th\u1eddi gian th\u1ef1c. Kh\u00e1c v\u1edbi HTTP truy\u1ec1n th\u1ed1ng theo m\u00f4 h\u00ecnh request-response v\u00e0 \u0111\u00f3ng k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i sau m\u1ed7i t\u01b0\u01a1ng t\u00e1c, WebSocket duy tr\u00ec m\u1ed9t k\u00eanh m\u1edf, trong \u0111\u00f3 c\u1ea3 client v\u00e0 server \u0111\u1ec1u c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 g\u1eedi tin nh\u1eafn cho nhau b\u1ea5t c\u1ee9 l\u00fac n\u00e0o.\n\n## WebSocket vs. HTTP: Nh\u1eefng kh\u00e1c bi\u1ec7t ch\u00ednh\n\n| T\u00ednh n\u0103ng | HTTP | WebSocket |\n| --------- | ------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------- |\n| K\u1ebft n\u1ed1i | Request-response, \u0111\u00f3ng sau m\u1ed7i request | Li\u00ean t\u1ee5c, lu\u00f4n m\u1edf |\n| Giao ti\u1ebfp | M\u1ed9t chi\u1ec1u (client y\u00eau c\u1ea7u, server ph\u1ea3n h\u1ed3i) | Hai chi\u1ec1u (c\u1ea3 hai c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 kh\u1edfi t\u1ea1o) |\n| Real-time | C\u1ea7n polling \u0111\u1ec3 c\u1eadp nh\u1eadt | H\u1ed7 tr\u1ee3 real-time t\u1ef1 nhi\u00ean |\n| Overhead | Cao (headers g\u1eedi v\u1edbi m\u1ed7i request) | Th\u1ea5p (sau handshake ban \u0111\u1ea7u) |\n\n## C\u00e1c tr\u01b0\u1eddng h\u1ee3p s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf\n\nWebSocket r\u1ea5t h\u1eefu \u00edch trong c\u00e1c \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng y\u00eau c\u1ea7u giao ti\u1ebfp hai chi\u1ec1u t\u1ee9c th\u1eddi:\n\n### 1. **\u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng Chat**\n\nNh\u1eafn tin th\u1eddi gian th\u1ef1c, ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng g\u1eedi v\u00e0 nh\u1eadn tin nh\u1eafn ngay l\u1eadp t\u1ee9c m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng c\u1ea7n t\u1ea3i l\u1ea1i trang.\n\n### 2. **Th\u00f4ng b\u00e1o Tr\u1ef1c ti\u1ebfp**\n\nPush notifications xu\u1ea5t hi\u1ec7n ngay khi c\u00f3 s\u1ef1 ki\u1ec7n x\u1ea3y ra tr\u00ean server.\n\n### 3. **Ch\u1ec9nh s\u1eeda C\u1ed9ng t\u00e1c**\n\n\u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng ki\u1ec3u Google Docs, nhi\u1ec1u ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng ch\u1ec9nh s\u1eeda c\u00f9ng l\u00fac v\u00e0 th\u1ea5y thay \u0111\u1ed5i c\u1ee7a nhau theo th\u1eddi gian th\u1ef1c.\n\n### 4. **Gaming**\n\nGame nhi\u1ec1u ng\u01b0\u1eddi ch\u01a1i y\u00eau c\u1ea7u giao ti\u1ebfp \u0111\u1ed9 tr\u1ec5 th\u1ea5p gi\u1eefa c\u00e1c ng\u01b0\u1eddi ch\u01a1i v\u00e0 server.\n\n### 5. **B\u1ea3ng gi\u00e1 C\u1ed5 phi\u1ebfu & Dashboard Tr\u1ef1c ti\u1ebfp**\n\n\u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng t\u00e0i ch\u00ednh hi\u1ec3n th\u1ecb c\u1eadp nh\u1eadt gi\u00e1 v\u00e0 d\u1eef li\u1ec7u th\u1ecb tr\u01b0\u1eddng theo th\u1eddi gian th\u1ef1c.\n\n## WebSocket ho\u1ea1t \u0111\u1ed9ng nh\u01b0 th\u1ebf n\u00e0o?\n\nV\u00f2ng \u0111\u1eddi WebSocket bao g\u1ed3m ba giai \u0111o\u1ea1n ch\u00ednh:\n\n### 1. **HTTP Handshake**\n\nK\u1ebft n\u1ed1i b\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u nh\u01b0 m\u1ed9t HTTP request ti\u00eau chu\u1ea9n v\u1edbi headers \u0111\u1eb7c bi\u1ec7t cho bi\u1ebft client mu\u1ed1n n\u00e2ng c\u1ea5p l\u00ean WebSocket:\n\n```\nGET /chat HTTP/1.1\nHost: example.com\nUpgrade: websocket\nConnection: Upgrade\n```\n\n### 2. **N\u00e2ng c\u1ea5p Giao th\u1ee9c**\n\nN\u1ebfu server h\u1ed7 tr\u1ee3 WebSocket, n\u00f3 ph\u1ea3n h\u1ed3i v\u1edbi status code 101, n\u00e2ng c\u1ea5p k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i t\u1eeb HTTP l\u00ean giao th\u1ee9c WebSocket.\n\n### 3. **K\u1ebft n\u1ed1i M\u1edf**\n\nSau khi n\u00e2ng c\u1ea5p, k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c gi\u1eef m\u1edf, v\u00e0 c\u1ea3 client v\u00e0 server \u0111\u1ec1u c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 g\u1eedi tin nh\u1eafn cho nhau b\u1ea5t c\u1ee9 l\u00fac n\u00e0o m\u00e0 kh\u00f4ng c\u00f3 overhead c\u1ee7a HTTP headers.\n\n## Socket.io vs. Native WebSocket\n\nKhi tri\u1ec3n khai WebSocket trong \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng, b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 hai l\u1ef1a ch\u1ecdn ch\u00ednh:\n\n### Socket.io\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- D\u1ec5 s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng v\u1edbi API \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n h\u01a1n\n- T\u1ef1 \u0111\u1ed9ng fallback sang long-polling n\u1ebfu WebSocket kh\u00f4ng kh\u1ea3 d\u1ee5ng\n- H\u1ed7 tr\u1ee3 s\u1eb5n rooms v\u00e0 namespaces\n- X\u1eed l\u00fd t\u1ef1 \u0111\u1ed9ng k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i l\u1ea1i\n- Kh\u1ea3 n\u0103ng broadcasting\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng:** H\u1ea7u h\u1ebft c\u00e1c \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng web, \u0111\u1eb7c bi\u1ec7t khi c\u1ea7n \u0111\u1ed9 tin c\u1eady tr\u00ean c\u00e1c tr\u00ecnh duy\u1ec7t v\u00e0 \u0111i\u1ec1u ki\u1ec7n m\u1ea1ng kh\u00e1c nhau.\n\n### Native WebSocket\n\n**\u01afu \u0111i\u1ec3m:**\n\n- Ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t nhi\u1ec1u h\u01a1n trong tri\u1ec3n khai\n- Nh\u1eb9 h\u01a1n (kh\u00f4ng c\u1ea7n th\u01b0 vi\u1ec7n b\u1ed5 sung)\n- Overhead th\u1ea5p h\u01a1n\n- API tr\u00ecnh duy\u1ec7t chu\u1ea9n\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng:** \u1ee8ng d\u1ee5ng quan tr\u1ecdng v\u1ec1 hi\u1ec7u n\u0103ng, c\u1ea7n ki\u1ec3m so\u00e1t \u0111\u1ea7y \u0111\u1ee7 v\u00e0 c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 x\u1eed l\u00fd c\u00e1c tr\u01b0\u1eddng h\u1ee3p \u0111\u1eb7c bi\u1ec7t th\u1ee7 c\u00f4ng.\n\n## B\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u nhanh: X\u00e2y d\u1ef1ng Chat \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n v\u1edbi Socket.io\n\n\u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 v\u00ed d\u1ee5 t\u1ed1i thi\u1ec3u v\u1ec1 \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng chat real-time s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng Socket.io:\n\n### Server (Node.js)\n\n```javascript\nconst express = require(\"express\");\nconst http = require(\"http\");\nconst socketIO = require(\"socket.io\");\n\nconst app = express();\nconst server = http.createServer(app);\nconst io = socketIO(server);\n\napp.use(express.static(\"public\"));\n\n// X\u1eed l\u00fd socket connections\nio.on(\"connection\", (socket) => {\n console.log(\"Ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng m\u1edbi k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i\");\n\n // L\u1eafng nghe tin nh\u1eafn chat\n socket.on(\"chat message\", (msg) => {\n // Broadcast tin nh\u1eafn t\u1edbi t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 clients \u0111\u00e3 k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i\n io.emit(\"chat message\", msg);\n });\n\n // X\u1eed l\u00fd ng\u1eaft k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i\n socket.on(\"disconnect\", () => {\n console.log(\"Ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng ng\u1eaft k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i\");\n });\n});\n\nconst PORT = process.env.PORT || 3000;\nserver.listen(PORT, () => {\n console.log(`Server \u0111ang ch\u1ea1y tr\u00ean port ${PORT}`);\n});\n```\n\n### Client (HTML + JavaScript)\n\n```html\n\n\n \n Chat \u0110\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n\n \n \n \n

    Ph\u00f2ng Chat \u0110\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n

    \n
      \n
      \n \n \n \n\n \n \n \n\n```\n\n### C\u00e0i \u0111\u1eb7t\n\n```bash\nnpm init -y\nnpm install express socket.io\nnode server.js\n```\n\nTruy c\u1eadp `http://localhost:3000` tr\u00ean nhi\u1ec1u tab tr\u00ecnh duy\u1ec7t \u0111\u1ec3 test chat!\n\n## Best Practices\n\n1. **X\u1eed l\u00fd K\u1ebft n\u1ed1i l\u1ea1i**: Lu\u00f4n tri\u1ec3n khai logic k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i l\u1ea1i cho c\u00e1c k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i b\u1ecb ng\u1eaft\n2. **Validate Messages**: Sanitize v\u00e0 validate t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 tin nh\u1eafn \u0111\u1ebfn tr\u00ean server\n3. **S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng Rooms**: T\u1ed5 ch\u1ee9c ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng th\u00e0nh c\u00e1c nh\u00f3m logic b\u1eb1ng Socket.io rooms\n4. **Gi\u00e1m s\u00e1t Hi\u1ec7u n\u0103ng**: Theo d\u00f5i s\u1ed1 l\u01b0\u1ee3ng k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i \u0111ang m\u1edf\n5. **Tri\u1ec3n khai Authentication**: B\u1ea3o m\u1eadt c\u00e1c k\u1ebft n\u1ed1i WebSocket v\u1edbi x\u00e1c th\u1ef1c ph\u00f9 h\u1ee3p\n\n## K\u1ebft lu\u1eadn\n\nWebSocket cung c\u1ea5p c\u00e1ch m\u1ea1nh m\u1ebd \u0111\u1ec3 x\u00e2y d\u1ef1ng \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng web real-time, t\u01b0\u01a1ng t\u00e1c. D\u00f9 b\u1ea1n ch\u1ecdn Socket.io cho s\u1ef1 ti\u1ec7n l\u1ee3i hay native WebSocket cho hi\u1ec7u n\u0103ng, vi\u1ec7c hi\u1ec3u c\u00f4ng ngh\u1ec7 n\u00e0y s\u1ebd m\u1edf ra kh\u1ea3 n\u0103ng t\u1ea1o tr\u1ea3i nghi\u1ec7m ng\u01b0\u1eddi d\u00f9ng h\u1ea5p d\u1eabn v\u1edbi c\u1eadp nh\u1eadt t\u1ee9c th\u1eddi v\u00e0 c\u1ed9ng t\u00e1c m\u01b0\u1ee3t m\u00e0.\n\nB\u1eaft \u0111\u1ea7u nh\u1ecf v\u1edbi chat ho\u1eb7c h\u1ec7 th\u1ed1ng th\u00f4ng b\u00e1o \u0111\u01a1n gi\u1ea3n, v\u00e0 b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd nhanh ch\u00f3ng th\u1ea5y WebSocket c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 bi\u1ebfn \u0111\u1ed5i \u1ee9ng d\u1ee5ng c\u1ee7a b\u1ea1n nh\u01b0 th\u1ebf n\u00e0o!\n\n---\n\n_Xu\u1ea5t b\u1ea3n: 17 th\u00e1ng 3, 2026_\n"}], "grading": null}, {"id": "typescript-utilities-with_skill", "prompt": "Create reference guide for TypeScript utility types", "eval_id": 8, "outputs": [{"name": "blog-post-en.md", "type": "text", "content": "# Complete Guide to TypeScript Utility Types: 10 Powerful Tools You Need to Know\n\n> **For developers who want to write safer and more flexible TypeScript code**\n\nHave you ever found yourself copy-pasting type definitions, recreating similar types, or rewriting interfaces just to change a few properties? TypeScript provides a powerful set of tools called **Utility Types** that help you transform and manipulate types in an elegant and type-safe manner.\n\nIn this comprehensive guide, we'll explore the 10 most important utility types, from basic to advanced, with practical examples and real-world scenarios you'll encounter in your daily development work.\n\n## TL;DR\n\nTypeScript Utility Types are built-in generic types that help transform types flexibly:\n\n| Utility Type | Purpose | Common Use Cases |\n| :--------------- | :--------------------------------------- | :----------------------------------- |\n| `Partial` | Makes all properties optional | Form updates, patches, configuration |\n| `Required` | Makes all properties required | Validation, type guards |\n| `Readonly` | Makes all properties readonly | Immutability, constants |\n| `Pick` | Selects specific properties | API responses, DTOs |\n| `Omit` | Excludes specific properties | Hiding sensitive data |\n| `Record` | Creates object type with keys and values | Maps, dictionaries, lookup tables |\n| `Exclude` | Removes types from union | Filtering types |\n| `Extract` | Extracts types from union | Type narrowing |\n| `NonNullable` | Removes null and undefined | Safe access, validation |\n| `ReturnType` | Gets return type of function | Type inference, composition |\n\n**When to use which?** See detailed comparison table in Part 4.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Making Properties Optional and Required\n\n### 1.1 Partial - When Everything Can Be Optional\n\n`Partial` makes all properties of a type optional. This is the most commonly used utility type.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Partial = {\n [P in keyof T]?: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n age: number;\n avatar: string;\n}\n\n// When updating user, only need some fields\nfunction updateUser(id: string, updates: Partial) {\n // \u2705 All valid\n // { name: \"New Name\" }\n // { email: \"new@email.com\", age: 25 }\n // { avatar: \"image.png\" }\n\n return fetch(`/api/users/${id}`, {\n method: \"PATCH\",\n body: JSON.stringify(updates),\n });\n}\n\n// Usage\nupdateUser(\"123\", { name: \"Alice\" }); // \u2705 OK\nupdateUser(\"123\", { email: \"alice@example.com\", age: 30 }); // \u2705 OK\nupdateUser(\"123\", { name: \"Bob\", unknownField: true }); // \u274c Error\n```\n\n**When to use Partial:**\n\n- Form updates and PATCH requests\n- Configuration objects with default values\n- Optional builder patterns\n- Incremental object construction\n\n---\n\n### 1.2 Required - Opposite of Partial\n\n`Required` makes all properties required, even if they were optional in the original type.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Required = {\n [P in keyof T]-?: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface DatabaseConfig {\n host?: string;\n port?: number;\n database?: string;\n username?: string;\n password?: string;\n}\n\n// When connecting, need to ensure all information is present\nfunction connectDatabase(config: Required) {\n // All properties are now required\n const connection = createConnection({\n host: config.host, // \u2705 Guaranteed to exist\n port: config.port, // \u2705 Guaranteed to exist\n database: config.database,\n user: config.username,\n password: config.password,\n });\n\n return connection;\n}\n\n// Type guard to convert from partial to required\nfunction validateConfig(\n config: DatabaseConfig,\n): config is Required {\n return !!(\n config.host &&\n config.port &&\n config.database &&\n config.username &&\n config.password\n );\n}\n\n// Usage\nconst config: DatabaseConfig = {\n host: \"localhost\",\n port: 5432,\n database: \"mydb\",\n};\n\nif (validateConfig(config)) {\n connectDatabase(config); // \u2705 OK - validated\n} else {\n throw new Error(\"Invalid configuration\");\n}\n```\n\n**When to use Required:**\n\n- Validation logic\n- Type guards\n- Converting partial configurations to complete\n- Ensuring completeness before processing\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Controlling Mutability\n\n### 2.1 Readonly - Immutability Enforcement\n\n`Readonly` makes all properties read-only, preventing accidental mutations.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Readonly = {\n readonly [P in keyof T]: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface AppConfig {\n apiUrl: string;\n apiKey: string;\n timeout: number;\n retries: number;\n}\n\n// Config should not change after initialization\nconst config: Readonly = {\n apiUrl: \"https://api.example.com\",\n apiKey: \"secret-key\",\n timeout: 5000,\n retries: 3,\n};\n\n// \u274c Error: Cannot assign to 'apiUrl' because it is a read-only property\nconfig.apiUrl = \"https://hacker.com\";\n\n// \u2705 Must create new object\nconst newConfig: Readonly = {\n ...config,\n timeout: 10000, // Only change timeout\n};\n```\n\n**Advanced use case - Readonly Arrays:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface TodoState {\n items: Readonly;\n filter: string;\n}\n\nfunction addTodo(state: TodoState, todo: Todo): TodoState {\n // \u274c Error: Cannot use push on readonly array\n // state.items.push(todo);\n\n // \u2705 Immutable update\n return {\n ...state,\n items: [...state.items, todo],\n };\n}\n```\n\n**When to use Readonly:**\n\n- Application config and constants\n- Redux/Zustand state objects\n- Functional programming patterns\n- Preventing accidental mutations\n- API response objects that shouldn't be modified\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Selecting and Excluding Properties\n\n### 3.1 Pick - Cherry-Picking Properties\n\n`Pick` allows you to select specific properties from a type.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Pick = {\n [P in K]: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n role: \"admin\" | \"user\";\n createdAt: Date;\n updatedAt: Date;\n}\n\n// Public profile - only show some fields\ntype PublicProfile = Pick;\n\n// API Response\ninterface ApiResponse {\n user: PublicProfile;\n token: string;\n}\n\nfunction createPublicProfile(user: User): PublicProfile {\n // \u2705 Type-safe selection\n return {\n id: user.id,\n name: user.name,\n email: user.email,\n };\n}\n\n// Login credentials\ntype LoginCredentials = Pick;\n\nfunction login(credentials: LoginCredentials) {\n // Only need email and password\n return authenticate(credentials.email, credentials.password);\n}\n```\n\n**When to use Pick:**\n\n- Creating DTOs (Data Transfer Objects)\n- API responses that don't expose all fields\n- Form types from larger models\n- Event payloads\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Omit - Excluding Properties\n\n`Omit` allows you to exclude specific properties from a type.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Omit = Pick>;\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n role: \"admin\" | \"user\";\n}\n\n// User creation - don't need id (auto-generated)\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\n\nfunction createUser(userData: CreateUserDto): User {\n return {\n id: generateId(),\n ...userData,\n };\n}\n\n// Safe user object - remove password\ntype SafeUser = Omit;\n\nfunction getUserProfile(userId: string): SafeUser {\n const user = database.users.find(userId);\n\n // Remove password before returning\n const { password, ...safeUser } = user;\n return safeUser;\n}\n\n// Multiple omissions\ntype PublicUser = Omit;\n```\n\n**Pick vs Omit - When to use which?**\n\n| Scenario | Use | Reason |\n| :--------------------------- | :----- | :--------------------------- |\n| Want fewer fields | `Pick` | Explicit about needed fields |\n| Want most fields, remove few | `Omit` | More concise |\n| Hiding sensitive data | `Omit` | Clear intent |\n| Creating DTOs | `Pick` | Explicit contract |\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Creating Object Types\n\n### 4.1 Record - Type-Safe Dictionaries\n\n`Record` creates an object type with keys of type `K` and values of type `T`.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Record = {\n [P in K]: T;\n};\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\n// HTTP Status codes mapping\ntype HttpStatusCode = 200 | 201 | 400 | 401 | 403 | 404 | 500;\n\nconst statusMessages: Record = {\n 200: \"OK\",\n 201: \"Created\",\n 400: \"Bad Request\",\n 401: \"Unauthorized\",\n 403: \"Forbidden\",\n 404: \"Not Found\",\n 500: \"Internal Server Error\",\n};\n\n// Translation dictionary\ntype Language = \"en\" | \"es\" | \"fr\" | \"de\" | \"ja\";\ntype TranslationKey = \"welcome\" | \"goodbye\" | \"hello\";\n\nconst translations: Record> = {\n en: {\n welcome: \"Welcome\",\n goodbye: \"Goodbye\",\n hello: \"Hello\",\n },\n es: {\n welcome: \"Bienvenido\",\n goodbye: \"Adi\u00f3s\",\n hello: \"Hola\",\n },\n fr: {\n welcome: \"Bienvenue\",\n goodbye: \"Au revoir\",\n hello: \"Bonjour\",\n },\n de: {\n welcome: \"Willkommen\",\n goodbye: \"Auf Wiedersehen\",\n hello: \"Hallo\",\n },\n ja: {\n welcome: \"\u3088\u3046\u3053\u305d\",\n goodbye: \"\u3055\u3088\u3046\u306a\u3089\",\n hello: \"\u3053\u3093\u306b\u3061\u306f\",\n },\n};\n\n// User permissions\ntype Permission = \"read\" | \"write\" | \"delete\" | \"admin\";\ntype Role = \"guest\" | \"user\" | \"moderator\" | \"admin\";\n\nconst rolePermissions: Record = {\n guest: [\"read\"],\n user: [\"read\", \"write\"],\n moderator: [\"read\", \"write\", \"delete\"],\n admin: [\"read\", \"write\", \"delete\", \"admin\"],\n};\n\nfunction hasPermission(role: Role, permission: Permission): boolean {\n return rolePermissions[role].includes(permission);\n}\n```\n\n**When to use Record:**\n\n- Lookup tables and mappings\n- Translation dictionaries\n- Configuration objects with known keys\n- State machines\n- API route handlers\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Working with Unions\n\n### 5.1 Exclude - Removing Types from Unions\n\n`Exclude` removes types from union type `T` that are assignable to `U`.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Exclude = T extends U ? never : T;\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\n// Primitive types filtering\ntype AllTypes = string | number | boolean | null | undefined;\ntype PrimitiveTypes = Exclude;\n// Result: string | number | boolean\n\n// Event types\ntype MouseEvent = \"click\" | \"dblclick\" | \"mousedown\" | \"mouseup\";\ntype KeyboardEvent = \"keydown\" | \"keyup\" | \"keypress\";\ntype AllEvents = MouseEvent | KeyboardEvent;\n\n// Only get mouse events\ntype OnlyMouseEvents = Exclude;\n// Result: 'click' | 'dblclick' | 'mousedown' | 'mouseup'\n\n// Function overload filtering\ntype ApiResponse =\n | { success: true; data: User }\n | { success: false; error: string }\n | { success: false; error: Error };\n\ntype SuccessResponse = Exclude;\n// Result: { success: true; data: User }\n\n// Excluding function types\ntype MixedTypes = string | number | (() => void) | (() => string);\ntype NonFunctionTypes = Exclude;\n// Result: string | number\n```\n\n**When to use Exclude:**\n\n- Filtering union types\n- Removing null/undefined from types\n- Type narrowing in conditional logic\n- Creating type variants\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Extract - Extracting Types from Unions\n\n`Extract` extracts types from union `T` that are assignable to `U`. It's the opposite of `Exclude`.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Extract = T extends U ? T : never;\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\n// Extracting specific types\ntype AllTypes = string | number | boolean | (() => void);\ntype OnlyFunctions = Extract;\n// Result: () => void\n\n// Status filtering\ntype Status = \"success\" | \"error\" | \"warning\" | \"info\" | \"loading\";\ntype AlertStatus = Extract;\n// Result: 'error' | 'warning'\n\n// API action types\ntype Action =\n | { type: \"SET_USER\"; payload: User }\n | { type: \"SET_TOKEN\"; payload: string }\n | { type: \"LOGOUT\" }\n | { type: \"REFRESH_TOKEN\"; payload: string };\n\n// Extract only actions with payload\ntype ActionsWithPayload = Extract;\n// Result:\n// | { type: 'SET_USER'; payload: User }\n// | { type: 'SET_TOKEN'; payload: string }\n// | { type: 'REFRESH_TOKEN'; payload: string }\n\n// Practical usage\nfunction handleActionWithPayload(action: ActionsWithPayload) {\n console.log(\"Processing payload:\", action.payload);\n // TypeScript knows action.payload exists\n}\n```\n\n**Extract vs Exclude:**\n\n| Use Case | Tool | Pattern |\n| :-------------------- | :---------------------- | :--------------------- |\n| Remove unwanted types | `Exclude` | \"Everything except...\" |\n| Get specific types | `Extract` | \"Only types that...\" |\n| Filter out primitives | `Exclude` | Type narrowing |\n| Get only primitives | `Extract` | Type selection |\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Null Safety\n\n### 6.1 NonNullable - Removing Null and Undefined\n\n`NonNullable` removes `null` and `undefined` from type `T`.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype NonNullable = T extends null | undefined ? never : T;\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\n// API response may be null\ninterface UserResponse {\n user: User | null;\n token: string | undefined;\n refreshToken?: string;\n}\n\n// Ensure non-null values\ntype SafeUserResponse = {\n [K in keyof UserResponse]: NonNullable;\n};\n// Result:\n// {\n// user: User;\n// token: string;\n// refreshToken: string;\n// }\n\n// Array filtering\nfunction filterNullable(array: (T | null | undefined)[]): NonNullable[] {\n return array.filter((item): item is NonNullable => item != null);\n}\n\nconst mixedArray = [\"hello\", null, \"world\", undefined, \"typescript\"];\nconst cleanArray = filterNullable(mixedArray);\n// Type: string[]\n// Value: ['hello', 'world', 'typescript']\n\n// Optional chaining safety\ninterface NestedData {\n user?: {\n profile?: {\n avatar?: string;\n };\n };\n}\n\nfunction getAvatarSafely(\n data: NestedData,\n): NonNullable | null {\n const avatar = data.user?.profile?.avatar;\n return avatar ?? null;\n}\n```\n\n**When to use NonNullable:**\n\n- After validation/type guards\n- Array filtering functions\n- Converting optional to required after check\n- API response processing\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Function Type Utilities\n\n### 7.1 ReturnType - Inferring Return Types\n\n`ReturnType` gets the return type of function type `T`.\n\n**Syntax:**\n\n```typescript\ntype ReturnType any> = T extends (\n ...args: any\n) => infer R\n ? R\n : any;\n```\n\n**Real-world example:**\n\n```typescript\n// API function\nasync function fetchUser(id: string) {\n const response = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);\n return response.json();\n}\n\n// Infer return type without duplication\ntype User = ReturnType;\n// Result: Promise (from response.json())\n\n// Better with explicit typing\nasync function fetchUserTyped(id: string): Promise<{\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n}> {\n const response = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);\n return response.json();\n}\n\ntype UserData = Awaited>;\n// Result: { id: string; name: string; email: string }\n\n// Factory functions\nfunction createStore(initialState: T) {\n let state = initialState;\n\n return {\n getState: () => state,\n setState: (newState: T) => {\n state = newState;\n },\n subscribe: (listener: (state: T) => void) => {\n // subscription logic\n },\n };\n}\n\ntype Store = ReturnType>;\n// Now we can use Store, Store, etc.\n\n// Callback type inference\nconst handlers = {\n onClick: (event: MouseEvent) => {\n console.log(\"Clicked:\", event.target);\n },\n onSubmit: (data: FormData) => {\n console.log(\"Submitted:\", data);\n return { success: true };\n },\n};\n\ntype SubmitResult = ReturnType;\n// Result: { success: boolean }\n```\n\n**Combining with other utilities:**\n\n```typescript\n// Get return type and make it partial\nfunction createUser(data: CreateUserDto) {\n return {\n id: generateId(),\n ...data,\n createdAt: new Date(),\n };\n}\n\ntype CreatedUser = ReturnType;\ntype PartialUser = Partial;\n\n// Array of return types\ntype HandlerResults = {\n [K in keyof typeof handlers]: ReturnType<(typeof handlers)[K]>;\n};\n```\n\n**When to use ReturnType:**\n\n- DRY principle - don't duplicate type definitions\n- Working with third-party libraries\n- Generic factory functions\n- Composing complex types from function signatures\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Real-World Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Building a Type-Safe API Client\n\n```typescript\n// Base API types\ninterface ApiEndpoint {\n method: \"GET\" | \"POST\" | \"PUT\" | \"PATCH\" | \"DELETE\";\n path: string;\n params?: Record;\n body?: unknown;\n}\n\n// Response wrapper\ninterface ApiResponse {\n data: T;\n status: number;\n message?: string;\n}\n\n// Define endpoints with utility types\ntype Endpoints = {\n getUser: {\n params: Pick;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n updateUser: {\n params: Pick;\n body: Partial>;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n createUser: {\n body: Required>;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n deleteUser: {\n params: Pick;\n response: ApiResponse<{ success: boolean }>;\n };\n};\n\n// Type-safe API client\nclass ApiClient {\n async request(\n endpoint: E,\n options: Endpoints[E] extends { params: infer P }\n ? { params: P }\n : Endpoints[E] extends { body: infer B }\n ? { body: B }\n : {},\n ): Promise {\n // Implementation\n return {} as any;\n }\n}\n\n// Usage - fully type-safe!\nconst client = new ApiClient();\n\nawait client.request(\"getUser\", {\n params: { id: \"123\" }, // \u2705 Type-safe\n});\n\nawait client.request(\"updateUser\", {\n params: { id: \"123\" },\n body: { name: \"Alice\" }, // \u2705 Partial update\n});\n\nawait client.request(\"createUser\", {\n body: {\n // \u2705 Must provide all required fields\n name: \"Bob\",\n email: \"bob@example.com\",\n password: \"secret\",\n },\n});\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: State Management with Type Utilities\n\n```typescript\n// Application state\ninterface AppState {\n user: User | null;\n isAuthenticated: boolean;\n theme: \"light\" | \"dark\";\n notifications: Notification[];\n settings: UserSettings;\n}\n\n// Actions\ntype StateAction = {\n type: `SET_${Uppercase}`;\n payload: AppState[K];\n};\n\n// Generate all possible actions\ntype Actions = {\n [K in keyof AppState]: StateAction;\n}[keyof AppState];\n\n// Reducer with type-safe updates\nfunction reducer(\n state: Readonly,\n action: Actions,\n): Readonly {\n // Pattern matching on action type\n if (action.type === \"SET_USER\") {\n return { ...state, user: action.payload };\n }\n // ... other cases\n return state;\n}\n\n// Selectors with ReturnType\nconst selectors = {\n getUser: (state: AppState) => state.user,\n isLoggedIn: (state: AppState) => state.isAuthenticated,\n getTheme: (state: AppState) => state.theme,\n};\n\ntype SelectorResults = {\n [K in keyof typeof selectors]: ReturnType<(typeof selectors)[K]>;\n};\n// Result:\n// {\n// getUser: User | null;\n// isLoggedIn: boolean;\n// getTheme: 'light' | 'dark';\n// }\n```\n\n### Scenario 3: Form Handling with Validation\n\n```typescript\n// Form data\ninterface RegistrationForm {\n username: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n confirmPassword: string;\n age: number;\n acceptTerms: boolean;\n}\n\n// Validation errors - all fields optional\ntype ValidationErrors = Partial>;\n\n// Form state\ninterface FormState {\n values: Partial;\n errors: ValidationErrors;\n touched: Partial>;\n isSubmitting: boolean;\n}\n\n// Field validator function type\ntype FieldValidator = (value: T) => string | undefined;\n\n// Validators for each field\nconst validators: Record> = {\n username: (value: string) =>\n value.length < 3 ? \"Username must be at least 3 characters\" : undefined,\n email: (value: string) =>\n !/\\S+@\\S+\\.\\S+/.test(value) ? \"Invalid email format\" : undefined,\n password: (value: string) =>\n value.length < 8 ? \"Password must be at least 8 characters\" : undefined,\n confirmPassword: (value: string) =>\n value !== formState.values.password ? \"Passwords must match\" : undefined,\n age: (value: number) =>\n value < 18 ? \"Must be at least 18 years old\" : undefined,\n acceptTerms: (value: boolean) =>\n !value ? \"You must accept terms and conditions\" : undefined,\n};\n\n// Submit handler - requires all fields\nasync function handleSubmit(\n data: Required,\n): Promise> {\n // All fields guaranteed to exist\n return apiClient.register(data);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 9: When to Use Which Utility Type\n\n### Decision Matrix\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 What do you want to do? \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502\n Modify Object Work with Unions\n \u2502 \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510 \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502 \u2502 \u2502\nMake Props Select/ Remove Extract\nOptional Exclude Types Types\n \u2502 Props \u2502 \u2502\n \u2502 \u2502 \u2502 \u2502\nPartial \u2502 Exclude Extract\n \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502\n Select Exclude\n Specific Specific\n \u2502 \u2502\nPick Omit\n```\n\n### Comparison Table - Quick Reference\n\n| Scenario | Tool Chain | Example |\n| :------------------------ | :------------------------------------ | :------------------------------------ |\n| **PATCH request body** | `Partial>` | Update user, exclude ID, all optional |\n| **Creation DTO** | `Omit` | New record, exclude auto-generated |\n| **Public API response** | `Pick` or `Omit` | Hide sensitive fields |\n| **Config with defaults** | `Partial` | User overrides default config |\n| **Validated form data** | `Required` | Ensure all fields present |\n| **Immutable state** | `Readonly` | Redux state, constants |\n| **Lookup table** | `Record` | Translation, mappings, enums |\n| **Non-null values** | `NonNullable` | After validation |\n| **Type from function** | `ReturnType` | DRY, infer from factory |\n| **Remove null/undefined** | `Exclude` | Union cleanup |\n\n### Best Practices Guidelines\n\n**1. Composition over Duplication**\n\n```typescript\n// \u274c Bad - Duplicating types\ninterface CreateUserDto {\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n}\n\ninterface UpdateUserDto {\n name?: string;\n email?: string;\n}\n\n// \u2705 Good - Using utility types\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n createdAt: Date;\n}\n\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\ntype UpdateUserDto = Partial>;\n```\n\n**2. Explicit over Implicit**\n\n```typescript\n// \u274c Unclear intent\ntype UserData = Omit;\n\n// \u2705 Clear intent\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\ntype UpdateUserPayload = Partial>;\n```\n\n**3. Type Guards with Utility Types**\n\n```typescript\nfunction isRequired(\n value: Partial,\n requiredKeys: (keyof T)[],\n): value is Required {\n return requiredKeys.every((key) => value[key] !== undefined);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 10: Advanced Patterns and Tips\n\n### Pattern 1: Conditional Property Types\n\n```typescript\n// Make specific properties optional\ntype PartialBy = Omit & Partial>;\n\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n age: number;\n}\n\ntype UserWithOptionalAge = PartialBy;\n// Result: { id: string; name: string; email: string; age?: number }\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Deep Readonly\n\n```typescript\ntype DeepReadonly = {\n readonly [P in keyof T]: T[P] extends object ? DeepReadonly : T[P];\n};\n\ninterface NestedConfig {\n api: {\n baseUrl: string;\n timeout: number;\n retries: {\n max: number;\n delay: number;\n };\n };\n}\n\nconst config: DeepReadonly = {\n api: {\n baseUrl: \"https://api.example.com\",\n timeout: 5000,\n retries: {\n max: 3,\n delay: 1000,\n },\n },\n};\n\n// \u274c All nested properties are readonly\n// config.api.retries.max = 5;\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Type-Safe Event Emitters\n\n```typescript\ntype EventMap = {\n \"user:login\": { userId: string; timestamp: Date };\n \"user:logout\": { userId: string };\n \"data:update\": { dataId: string; changes: Record };\n};\n\nclass TypedEventEmitter {\n on(\n event: K,\n handler: (payload: EventMap[K]) => void,\n ): void {\n // Implementation\n }\n\n emit(event: K, payload: EventMap[K]): void {\n // Implementation\n }\n}\n\nconst emitter = new TypedEventEmitter();\n\n// \u2705 Type-safe\nemitter.on(\"user:login\", (payload) => {\n console.log(payload.userId); // payload type inferred correctly\n});\n\n// \u274c Type error\nemitter.emit(\"user:login\", { wrongField: \"value\" });\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Takeaways\n\n1. **Partial and Required** are the perfect pair for form handling and validation\n2. **Readonly** is a must-have for immutable patterns and configuration\n3. **Pick vs Omit** - choose based on the number of properties to include/exclude\n4. **Record** is the go-to for lookup tables and type-safe dictionaries\n5. **Exclude/Extract** are powerful for union manipulation\n6. **NonNullable** is a safety net after validation\n7. **ReturnType** helps with DRY and type inference from functions\n8. **Composition** - combine utilities to create complex types\n9. **Type Guards** - always validate before using Required types\n10. **Naming Conventions** - use clear names to express intent\n\n## Conclusion\n\nTypeScript Utility Types are not just syntactic sugar - they're essential tools that help you write type-safe code with less duplication and better maintainability. By mastering these 10 utilities, you can:\n\n- \u2705 Eliminate type duplication\n- \u2705 Build type-safe APIs and data layers\n- \u2705 Enforce immutability and correctness\n- \u2705 Create flexible, reusable type definitions\n- \u2705 Improve developer experience with better autocomplete\n\n**Next Steps:**\n\n1. Practice with the examples in this guide\n2. Refactor existing code to use utility types\n3. Explore advanced patterns like conditional types\n4. Check the official TypeScript documentation for more utilities\n5. Share this knowledge with your team!\n\n**Resources:**\n\n- [TypeScript Handbook - Utility Types](https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/utility-types.html)\n- [TypeScript Deep Dive](https://basarat.gitbook.io/typescript/)\n- [Type Challenges](https://github.com/type-challenges/type-challenges)\n- [TypeScript Playground](https://www.typescriptlang.org/play)\n\n---\n\n_Happy typing! \ud83d\ude80_\n"}, {"name": "blog-post-vi.md", "type": "text", "content": "# H\u01b0\u1edbng D\u1eabn \u0110\u1ea7y \u0110\u1ee7 v\u1ec1 TypeScript Utility Types: 10 C\u00f4ng C\u1ee5 M\u1ea1nh M\u1ebd B\u1ea1n C\u1ea7n Bi\u1ebft\n\n> **D\u00e0nh cho c\u00e1c developer mu\u1ed1n vi\u1ebft TypeScript code an to\u00e0n v\u00e0 linh ho\u1ea1t h\u01a1n**\n\nB\u1ea1n \u0111\u00e3 bao gi\u1edd ph\u1ea3i copy-paste type definitions, t\u1ea1o l\u1ea1i types t\u01b0\u01a1ng t\u1ef1 nhau, hay vi\u1ebft \u0111i vi\u1ebft l\u1ea1i c\u00e1c interface ch\u1ec9 \u0111\u1ec3 thay \u0111\u1ed5i v\u00e0i properties? TypeScript cung c\u1ea5p m\u1ed9t b\u1ed9 c\u00f4ng c\u1ee5 m\u1ea1nh m\u1ebd g\u1ecdi l\u00e0 **Utility Types** gi\u00fap b\u1ea1n transform v\u00e0 manipulate types m\u1ed9t c\u00e1ch elegant v\u00e0 type-safe.\n\nTrong h\u01b0\u1edbng d\u1eabn n\u00e0y, ch\u00fang ta s\u1ebd kh\u00e1m ph\u00e1 10 utility types quan tr\u1ecdng nh\u1ea5t, t\u1eeb c\u01a1 b\u1ea3n \u0111\u1ebfn n\u00e2ng cao, v\u1edbi c\u00e1c v\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf v\u00e0 scenarios m\u00e0 b\u1ea1n s\u1ebd g\u1eb7p trong c\u00f4ng vi\u1ec7c h\u00e0ng ng\u00e0y.\n\n## TL;DR\n\nTypeScript Utility Types l\u00e0 c\u00e1c generic types built-in gi\u00fap transform types m\u1ed9t c\u00e1ch linh ho\u1ea1t:\n\n| Utility Type | M\u1ee5c \u0110\u00edch | Use Case Ph\u1ed5 Bi\u1ebfn |\n| :--------------- | :------------------------------------ | :----------------------------------- |\n| `Partial` | Bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties th\u00e0nh optional | Form updates, patches, configuration |\n| `Required` | Bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties th\u00e0nh required | Validation, type guards |\n| `Readonly` | Bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties th\u00e0nh readonly | Immutability, constants |\n| `Pick` | Ch\u1ecdn specific properties | API responses, DTOs |\n| `Omit` | Lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf specific properties | Hiding sensitive data |\n| `Record` | T\u1ea1o object type v\u1edbi keys v\u00e0 values | Maps, dictionaries, lookup tables |\n| `Exclude` | Lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf types t\u1eeb union | Filtering types |\n| `Extract` | Tr\u00edch xu\u1ea5t types t\u1eeb union | Type narrowing |\n| `NonNullable` | Lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf null v\u00e0 undefined | Safe access, validation |\n| `ReturnType` | L\u1ea5y return type c\u1ee7a function | Type inference, composition |\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng c\u00e1i n\u00e0o?** Xem b\u1ea3ng so s\u00e1nh chi ti\u1ebft \u1edf Ph\u1ea7n 4.\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 1: Making Properties Optional and Required\n\n### 1.1 Partial - Khi M\u1ecdi Th\u1ee9 C\u00f3 Th\u1ec3 Optional\n\n`Partial` bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties c\u1ee7a m\u1ed9t type th\u00e0nh optional. \u0110\u00e2y l\u00e0 utility type \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c s\u1eed d\u1ee5ng nhi\u1ec1u nh\u1ea5t.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Partial = {\n [P in keyof T]?: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n age: number;\n avatar: string;\n}\n\n// Khi update user, ch\u1ec9 c\u1ea7n m\u1ed9t s\u1ed1 fields\nfunction updateUser(id: string, updates: Partial) {\n // \u2705 T\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 \u0111\u1ec1u h\u1ee3p l\u1ec7\n // { name: \"New Name\" }\n // { email: \"new@email.com\", age: 25 }\n // { avatar: \"image.png\" }\n\n return fetch(`/api/users/${id}`, {\n method: \"PATCH\",\n body: JSON.stringify(updates),\n });\n}\n\n// S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng\nupdateUser(\"123\", { name: \"Alice\" }); // \u2705 OK\nupdateUser(\"123\", { email: \"alice@example.com\", age: 30 }); // \u2705 OK\nupdateUser(\"123\", { name: \"Bob\", unknownField: true }); // \u274c Error\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Partial:**\n\n- Form updates v\u00e0 PATCH requests\n- Configuration objects v\u1edbi default values\n- Optional builder patterns\n- Incremental object construction\n\n---\n\n### 1.2 Required - Opposite c\u1ee7a Partial\n\n`Required` bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties th\u00e0nh required, ngay c\u1ea3 khi ch\u00fang optional \u1edf type g\u1ed1c.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Required = {\n [P in keyof T]-?: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface DatabaseConfig {\n host?: string;\n port?: number;\n database?: string;\n username?: string;\n password?: string;\n}\n\n// Khi connect, c\u1ea7n \u0111\u1ea3m b\u1ea3o c\u00f3 t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 th\u00f4ng tin\nfunction connectDatabase(config: Required) {\n // T\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties b\u00e2y gi\u1edd \u0111\u1ec1u required\n const connection = createConnection({\n host: config.host, // \u2705 Guaranteed to exist\n port: config.port, // \u2705 Guaranteed to exist\n database: config.database,\n user: config.username,\n password: config.password,\n });\n\n return connection;\n}\n\n// Type guard \u0111\u1ec3 convert t\u1eeb partial sang required\nfunction validateConfig(\n config: DatabaseConfig,\n): config is Required {\n return !!(\n config.host &&\n config.port &&\n config.database &&\n config.username &&\n config.password\n );\n}\n\n// S\u1eed d\u1ee5ng\nconst config: DatabaseConfig = {\n host: \"localhost\",\n port: 5432,\n database: \"mydb\",\n};\n\nif (validateConfig(config)) {\n connectDatabase(config); // \u2705 OK - validated\n} else {\n throw new Error(\"Invalid configuration\");\n}\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Required:**\n\n- Validation logic\n- Type guards\n- Converting partial configurations th\u00e0nh complete\n- Ensuring completeness tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi processing\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 2: Controlling Mutability\n\n### 2.1 Readonly - Immutability Enforcement\n\n`Readonly` bi\u1ebfn t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 properties th\u00e0nh read-only, preventing accidental mutations.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Readonly = {\n readonly [P in keyof T]: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface AppConfig {\n apiUrl: string;\n apiKey: string;\n timeout: number;\n retries: number;\n}\n\n// Config kh\u00f4ng \u0111\u01b0\u1ee3c thay \u0111\u1ed5i sau khi initialize\nconst config: Readonly = {\n apiUrl: \"https://api.example.com\",\n apiKey: \"secret-key\",\n timeout: 5000,\n retries: 3,\n};\n\n// \u274c Error: Cannot assign to 'apiUrl' because it is a read-only property\nconfig.apiUrl = \"https://hacker.com\";\n\n// \u2705 Ph\u1ea3i t\u1ea1o new object\nconst newConfig: Readonly = {\n ...config,\n timeout: 10000, // Ch\u1ec9 thay \u0111\u1ed5i timeout\n};\n```\n\n**Use case n\u00e2ng cao - Readonly Arrays:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface TodoState {\n items: Readonly;\n filter: string;\n}\n\nfunction addTodo(state: TodoState, todo: Todo): TodoState {\n // \u274c Error: Cannot use push on readonly array\n // state.items.push(todo);\n\n // \u2705 Immutable update\n return {\n ...state,\n items: [...state.items, todo],\n };\n}\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Readonly:**\n\n- Application config v\u00e0 constants\n- Redux/Zustand state objects\n- Functional programming patterns\n- Preventing accidental mutations\n- API response objects kh\u00f4ng n\u00ean modify\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 3: Selecting and Excluding Properties\n\n### 3.1 Pick - Cherry-Picking Properties\n\n`Pick` cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n select specific properties t\u1eeb m\u1ed9t type.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Pick = {\n [P in K]: T[P];\n};\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n role: \"admin\" | \"user\";\n createdAt: Date;\n updatedAt: Date;\n}\n\n// Public profile - ch\u1ec9 show m\u1ed9t s\u1ed1 fields\ntype PublicProfile = Pick;\n\n// API Response\ninterface ApiResponse {\n user: PublicProfile;\n token: string;\n}\n\nfunction createPublicProfile(user: User): PublicProfile {\n // \u2705 Type-safe selection\n return {\n id: user.id,\n name: user.name,\n email: user.email,\n };\n}\n\n// Login credentials\ntype LoginCredentials = Pick;\n\nfunction login(credentials: LoginCredentials) {\n // Ch\u1ec9 c\u1ea7n email v\u00e0 password\n return authenticate(credentials.email, credentials.password);\n}\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Pick:**\n\n- Creating DTOs (Data Transfer Objects)\n- API responses kh\u00f4ng mu\u1ed1n expose t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 fields\n- Form types t\u1eeb larger models\n- Event payloads\n\n---\n\n### 3.2 Omit - Excluding Properties\n\n`Omit` cho ph\u00e9p b\u1ea1n lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf specific properties t\u1eeb m\u1ed9t type.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Omit = Pick>;\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n role: \"admin\" | \"user\";\n}\n\n// User creation - kh\u00f4ng c\u1ea7n id (auto-generated)\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\n\nfunction createUser(userData: CreateUserDto): User {\n return {\n id: generateId(),\n ...userData,\n };\n}\n\n// Safe user object - lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf password\ntype SafeUser = Omit;\n\nfunction getUserProfile(userId: string): SafeUser {\n const user = database.users.find(userId);\n\n // Remove password before returning\n const { password, ...safeUser } = user;\n return safeUser;\n}\n\n// Multiple omissions\ntype PublicUser = Omit;\n```\n\n**Pick vs Omit - Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng c\u00e1i n\u00e0o?**\n\n| Scenario | D\u00f9ng | L\u00fd do |\n| :---------------------------- | :----- | :--------------------- |\n| Mu\u1ed1n \u00edt fields h\u01a1n | `Pick` | Explicit v\u1ec1 fields c\u1ea7n |\n| Mu\u1ed1n nhi\u1ec1u fields, b\u1ecf v\u00e0i c\u00e1i | `Omit` | Ng\u1eafn g\u1ecdn h\u01a1n |\n| Hiding sensitive data | `Omit` | Clear intent |\n| Creating DTOs | `Pick` | Explicit contract |\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 4: Creating Object Types\n\n### 4.1 Record - Type-Safe Dictionaries\n\n`Record` t\u1ea1o object type v\u1edbi keys type `K` v\u00e0 values type `T`.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Record = {\n [P in K]: T;\n};\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\n// HTTP Status codes mapping\ntype HttpStatusCode = 200 | 201 | 400 | 401 | 403 | 404 | 500;\n\nconst statusMessages: Record = {\n 200: \"OK\",\n 201: \"Created\",\n 400: \"Bad Request\",\n 401: \"Unauthorized\",\n 403: \"Forbidden\",\n 404: \"Not Found\",\n 500: \"Internal Server Error\",\n};\n\n// Translation dictionary\ntype Language = \"en\" | \"vi\" | \"ja\";\ntype TranslationKey = \"welcome\" | \"goodbye\" | \"hello\";\n\nconst translations: Record> = {\n en: {\n welcome: \"Welcome\",\n goodbye: \"Goodbye\",\n hello: \"Hello\",\n },\n vi: {\n welcome: \"Ch\u00e0o m\u1eebng\",\n goodbye: \"T\u1ea1m bi\u1ec7t\",\n hello: \"Xin ch\u00e0o\",\n },\n ja: {\n welcome: \"\u3088\u3046\u3053\u305d\",\n goodbye: \"\u3055\u3088\u3046\u306a\u3089\",\n hello: \"\u3053\u3093\u306b\u3061\u306f\",\n },\n};\n\n// User permissions\ntype Permission = \"read\" | \"write\" | \"delete\" | \"admin\";\ntype Role = \"guest\" | \"user\" | \"moderator\" | \"admin\";\n\nconst rolePermissions: Record = {\n guest: [\"read\"],\n user: [\"read\", \"write\"],\n moderator: [\"read\", \"write\", \"delete\"],\n admin: [\"read\", \"write\", \"delete\", \"admin\"],\n};\n\nfunction hasPermission(role: Role, permission: Permission): boolean {\n return rolePermissions[role].includes(permission);\n}\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Record:**\n\n- Lookup tables v\u00e0 mappings\n- Translation dictionaries\n- Configuration objects v\u1edbi known keys\n- State machines\n- API route handlers\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 5: Working with Unions\n\n### 5.1 Exclude - Removing Types from Unions\n\n`Exclude` lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf types t\u1eeb union type `T` m\u00e0 assignable to `U`.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Exclude = T extends U ? never : T;\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\n// Primitive types filtering\ntype AllTypes = string | number | boolean | null | undefined;\ntype PrimitiveTypes = Exclude;\n// Result: string | number | boolean\n\n// Event types\ntype MouseEvent = \"click\" | \"dblclick\" | \"mousedown\" | \"mouseup\";\ntype KeyboardEvent = \"keydown\" | \"keyup\" | \"keypress\";\ntype AllEvents = MouseEvent | KeyboardEvent;\n\n// Ch\u1ec9 l\u1ea5y mouse events\ntype OnlyMouseEvents = Exclude;\n// Result: 'click' | 'dblclick' | 'mousedown' | 'mouseup'\n\n// Function overload filtering\ntype ApiResponse =\n | { success: true; data: User }\n | { success: false; error: string }\n | { success: false; error: Error };\n\ntype SuccessResponse = Exclude;\n// Result: { success: true; data: User }\n\n// Excluding function types\ntype MixedTypes = string | number | (() => void) | (() => string);\ntype NonFunctionTypes = Exclude;\n// Result: string | number\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng Exclude:**\n\n- Filtering union types\n- Removing null/undefined t\u1eeb types\n- Type narrowing trong conditional logic\n- Creating type variants\n\n---\n\n### 5.2 Extract - Extracting Types from Unions\n\n`Extract` tr\u00edch xu\u1ea5t types t\u1eeb union `T` m\u00e0 assignable to `U`. Opposite c\u1ee7a `Exclude`.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype Extract = T extends U ? T : never;\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\n// Extracting specific types\ntype AllTypes = string | number | boolean | (() => void);\ntype OnlyFunctions = Extract;\n// Result: () => void\n\n// Status filtering\ntype Status = \"success\" | \"error\" | \"warning\" | \"info\" | \"loading\";\ntype AlertStatus = Extract;\n// Result: 'error' | 'warning'\n\n// API action types\ntype Action =\n | { type: \"SET_USER\"; payload: User }\n | { type: \"SET_TOKEN\"; payload: string }\n | { type: \"LOGOUT\" }\n | { type: \"REFRESH_TOKEN\"; payload: string };\n\n// Extract ch\u1ec9 actions c\u00f3 payload\ntype ActionsWithPayload = Extract;\n// Result:\n// | { type: 'SET_USER'; payload: User }\n// | { type: 'SET_TOKEN'; payload: string }\n// | { type: 'REFRESH_TOKEN'; payload: string }\n\n// Practical usage\nfunction handleActionWithPayload(action: ActionsWithPayload) {\n console.log(\"Processing payload:\", action.payload);\n // TypeScript knows action.payload exists\n}\n```\n\n**Extract vs Exclude:**\n\n| Use Case | Tool | Pattern |\n| :-------------------- | :---------------------- | :--------------------- |\n| Remove unwanted types | `Exclude` | \"Everything except...\" |\n| Get specific types | `Extract` | \"Only types that...\" |\n| Filter out primitives | `Exclude` | Type narrowing |\n| Get only primitives | `Extract` | Type selection |\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 6: Null Safety\n\n### 6.1 NonNullable - Removing Null and Undefined\n\n`NonNullable` lo\u1ea1i b\u1ecf `null` v\u00e0 `undefined` t\u1eeb type `T`.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype NonNullable = T extends null | undefined ? never : T;\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\n// API response c\u00f3 th\u1ec3 null\ninterface UserResponse {\n user: User | null;\n token: string | undefined;\n refreshToken?: string;\n}\n\n// Ensure non-null values\ntype SafeUserRespo = {\n [K in keyof UserResponse]: NonNullable;\n};\n// Result:\n// {\n// user: User;\n// token: string;\n// refreshToken: string;\n// }\n\n// Array filtering\nfunction filterNullable(array: (T | null | undefined)[]): NonNullable[] {\n return array.filter((item): item is NonNullable => item != null);\n}\n\nconst mixedArray = [\"hello\", null, \"world\", undefined, \"typescript\"];\nconst cleanArray = filterNullable(mixedArray);\n// Type: string[]\n// Value: ['hello', 'world', 'typescript']\n\n// Optional chaining safety\ninterface NestedData {\n user?: {\n profile?: {\n avatar?: string;\n };\n };\n}\n\nfunction getAvatarSafely(\n data: NestedData,\n): NonNullable | null {\n const avatar = data.user?.profile?.avatar;\n return avatar ?? null;\n}\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng NonNullable:**\n\n- After validation/type guards\n- Array filtering functions\n- Converting optional to required sau khi check\n- API response processing\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 7: Function Type Utilities\n\n### 7.1 ReturnType - Inferring Return Types\n\n`ReturnType` l\u1ea5y return type c\u1ee7a function type `T`.\n\n**C\u00fa ph\u00e1p:**\n\n```typescript\ntype ReturnType any> = T extends (\n ...args: any\n) => infer R\n ? R\n : any;\n```\n\n**V\u00ed d\u1ee5 th\u1ef1c t\u1ebf:**\n\n```typescript\n// API function\nasync function fetchUser(id: string) {\n const response = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);\n return response.json();\n}\n\n// Infer return type without duplication\ntype User = ReturnType;\n// Result: Promise (t\u1eeb response.json())\n\n// Better v\u1edbi explicit typing\nasync function fetchUserTyped(id: string): Promise<{\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n}> {\n const response = await fetch(`/api/users/${id}`);\n return response.json();\n}\n\ntype UserData = Awaited>;\n// Result: { id: string; name: string; email: string }\n\n// Factory functions\nfunction createStore(initialState: T) {\n let state = initialState;\n\n return {\n getState: () => state,\n setState: (newState: T) => {\n state = newState;\n },\n subscribe: (listener: (state: T) => void) => {\n // subscription logic\n },\n };\n}\n\ntype Store = ReturnType>;\n// Now we can use Store, Store, etc.\n\n// Callback type inference\nconst handlers = {\n onClick: (event: MouseEvent) => {\n console.log(\"Clicked:\", event.target);\n },\n onSubmit: (data: FormData) => {\n console.log(\"Submitted:\", data);\n return { success: true };\n },\n};\n\ntype SubmitResult = ReturnType;\n// Result: { success: boolean }\n```\n\n**Combining v\u1edbi c\u00e1c utilities kh\u00e1c:**\n\n```typescript\n// Get return type v\u00e0 make it partial\nfunction createUser(data: CreateUserDto) {\n return {\n id: generateId(),\n ...data,\n createdAt: new Date(),\n };\n}\n\ntype CreatedUser = ReturnType;\ntype PartialUser = Partial;\n\n// Array of return types\ntype HandlerResults = {\n [K in keyof typeof handlers]: ReturnType<(typeof handlers)[K]>;\n};\n```\n\n**Khi n\u00e0o d\u00f9ng ReturnType:**\n\n- DRY principle - kh\u00f4ng duplicate type definitions\n- Working with third-party libraries\n- Generic factory functions\n- Composing complex types t\u1eeb function signatures\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 8: Real-World Scenarios\n\n### Scenario 1: Building a Type-Safe API Client\n\n```typescript\n// Base API types\ninterface ApiEndpoint {\n method: \"GET\" | \"POST\" | \"PUT\" | \"PATCH\" | \"DELETE\";\n path: string;\n params?: Record;\n body?: unknown;\n}\n\n// Response wrapper\ninterface ApiResponse {\n data: T;\n status: number;\n message?: string;\n}\n\n// Define endpoints v\u1edbi utility types\ntype Endpoints = {\n getUser: {\n params: Pick;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n updateUser: {\n params: Pick;\n body: Partial>;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n createUser: {\n body: Required>;\n response: ApiResponse;\n };\n deleteUser: {\n params: Pick;\n response: ApiResponse<{ success: boolean }>;\n };\n};\n\n// Type-safe API client\nclass ApiClient {\n async request(\n endpoint: E,\n options: Endpoints[E] extends { params: infer P }\n ? { params: P }\n : Endpoints[E] extends { body: infer B }\n ? { body: B }\n : {},\n ): Promise {\n // Implementation\n return {} as any;\n }\n}\n\n// Usage - fully type-safe!\nconst client = new ApiClient();\n\nawait client.request(\"getUser\", {\n params: { id: \"123\" }, // \u2705 Type-safe\n});\n\nawait client.request(\"updateUser\", {\n params: { id: \"123\" },\n body: { name: \"Alice\" }, // \u2705 Partial update\n});\n\nawait client.request(\"createUser\", {\n body: {\n // \u2705 Must provide all required fields\n name: \"Bob\",\n email: \"bob@example.com\",\n password: \"secret\",\n },\n});\n```\n\n### Scenario 2: State Management v\u1edbi Type Utilities\n\n```typescript\n// Application state\ninterface AppState {\n user: User | null;\n isAuthenticated: boolean;\n theme: \"light\" | \"dark\";\n notifications: Notification[];\n settings: UserSettings;\n}\n\n// Actions\ntype StateAction = {\n type: `SET_${Uppercase}`;\n payload: AppState[K];\n};\n\n// Generate all possible actions\ntype Actions = {\n [K in keyof AppState]: StateAction;\n}[keyof AppState];\n\n// Reducer v\u1edbi type-safe updates\nfunction reducer(\n state: Readonly,\n action: Actions,\n): Readonly {\n // Pattern matching on action type\n if (action.type === \"SET_USER\") {\n return { ...state, user: action.payload };\n }\n // ... other cases\n return state;\n}\n\n// Selectors v\u1edbi ReturnType\nconst selectors = {\n getUser: (state: AppState) => state.user,\n isLoggedIn: (state: AppState) => state.isAuthenticated,\n getTheme: (state: AppState) => state.theme,\n};\n\ntype SelectorResults = {\n [K in keyof typeof selectors]: ReturnType<(typeof selectors)[K]>;\n};\n// Result:\n// {\n// getUser: User | null;\n// isLoggedIn: boolean;\n// getTheme: 'light' | 'dark';\n// }\n```\n\n### Scenario 3: Form Handling v\u1edbi Validation\n\n```typescript\n// Form data\ninterface RegistrationForm {\n username: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n confirmPassword: string;\n age: number;\n acceptTerms: boolean;\n}\n\n// Validation errors - t\u1ea5t c\u1ea3 fields optional\ntype ValidationErrors = Partial>;\n\n// Form state\ninterface FormState {\n values: Partial;\n errors: ValidationErrors;\n touched: Partial>;\n isSubmitting: boolean;\n}\n\n// Field validator function type\ntype FieldValidator = (value: T) => string | undefined;\n\n// Validators cho t\u1eebng field\nconst validators: Record> = {\n username: (value: string) =>\n value.length < 3 ? \"Username must be at least 3 characters\" : undefined,\n email: (value: string) =>\n !/\\S+@\\S+\\.\\S+/.test(value) ? \"Invalid email format\" : undefined,\n password: (value: string) =>\n value.length < 8 ? \"Password must be at least 8 characters\" : undefined,\n confirmPassword: (value: string) =>\n value !== formState.values.password ? \"Passwords must match\" : undefined,\n age: (value: number) =>\n value < 18 ? \"Must be at least 18 years old\" : undefined,\n acceptTerms: (value: boolean) =>\n !value ? \"You must accept terms and conditions\" : undefined,\n};\n\n// Submit handler - requires all fields\nasync function handleSubmit(\n data: Required,\n): Promise> {\n // All fields guaranteed to exist\n return apiClient.register(data);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 9: When to Use Which Utility Type\n\n### Decision Matrix\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n\u2502 B\u1ea1n mu\u1ed1n l\u00e0m g\u00ec? \u2502\n\u2514\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2518\n \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502\n Modify Object Work with Unions\n \u2502 \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510 \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502 \u2502 \u2502\nMake Props Select/ Remove Extract\nOptional Exclude Types Types\n \u2502 Props \u2502 \u2502\n \u2502 \u2502 \u2502 \u2502\nPartial \u2502 Exclude Extract\n \u2502\n \u250c\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2534\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2510\n \u2502 \u2502\n Select Exclude\n Specific Specific\n \u2502 \u2502\nPick Omit\n```\n\n### Comparison Table - Quick Reference\n\n| Scenario | Tool Chain | Example |\n| :------------------------ | :-------------------------------------- | :------------------------------------ |\n| **PATCH request body** | `Partial>` | Update user, exclude ID, all optional |\n| **Creation DTO** | `Omit` | New record, exclude auto-generated |\n| **Public API response** | `Pick` ho\u1eb7c `Omit` | Hide sensitive fields |\n| **Config with defaults** | `Partial` | User overrides default config |\n| **Validated form data** | `Required` | Ensure all fields present |\n| **Immutable state** | `Readonly` | Redux state, constants |\n| **Lookup table** | `Record` | Translation, mappings, enums |\n| **Non-null values** | `NonNullable` | After validation |\n| **Type from function** | `ReturnType` | DRY, infer from factory |\n| **Remove null/undefined** | `Exclude` | Union cleanup |\n\n### Best Practices Guidelines\n\n**1. Composition over Duplication**\n\n```typescript\n// \u274c Bad - Duplicating types\ninterface CreateUserDto {\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n}\n\ninterface UpdateUserDto {\n name?: string;\n email?: string;\n}\n\n// \u2705 Good - Using utility types\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n password: string;\n createdAt: Date;\n}\n\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\ntype UpdateUserDto = Partial>;\n```\n\n**2. Explicit over Implicit**\n\n```typescript\n// \u274c Unclear intent\ntype UserData = Omit;\n\n// \u2705 Clear intent\ntype CreateUserDto = Omit;\ntype UpdateUserPayload = Partial>;\n```\n\n**3. Type Guards v\u1edbi Utility Types**\n\n```typescript\nfunction isRequired(\n value: Partial,\n requiredKeys: (keyof T)[],\n): value is Required {\n return requiredKeys.every((key) => value[key] !== undefined);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Ph\u1ea7n 10: Advanced Patterns v\u00e0 Tips\n\n### Pattern 1: Conditional Property Types\n\n```typescript\n// Make specific properties optional\ntype PartialBy = Omit & Partial>;\n\ninterface User {\n id: string;\n name: string;\n email: string;\n age: number;\n}\n\ntype UserWithOptionalAge = PartialBy;\n// Result: { id: string; name: string; email: string; age?: number }\n```\n\n### Pattern 2: Deep Readonly\n\n```typescript\ntype DeepReadonly = {\n readonly [P in keyof T]: T[P] extends object ? DeepReadonly : T[P];\n};\n\ninterface NestedConfig {\n api: {\n baseUrl: string;\n timeout: number;\n retries: {\n max: number;\n delay: number;\n };\n };\n}\n\nconst config: DeepReadonly = {\n api: {\n baseUrl: \"https://api.example.com\",\n timeout: 5000,\n retries: {\n max: 3,\n delay: 1000,\n },\n },\n};\n\n// \u274c All nested properties are readonly\n// config.api.retries.max = 5;\n```\n\n### Pattern 3: Type-Safe Event Emitters\n\n```typescript\ntype EventMap = {\n \"user:login\": { userId: string; timestamp: Date };\n \"user:logout\": { userId: string };\n \"data:update\": { dataId: string; changes: Record };\n};\n\nclass TypedEventEmitter {\n on(\n event: K,\n handler: (payload: EventMap[K]) => void,\n ): void {\n // Implementation\n }\n\n emit(event: K, payload: EventMap[K]): void {\n // Implementation\n }\n}\n\nconst emitter = new TypedEventEmitter();\n\n// \u2705 Type-safe\nemitter.on(\"user:login\", (payload) => {\n console.log(payload.userId); // payload type inferred correctly\n});\n\n// \u274c Type error\nemitter.emit(\"user:login\", { wrongField: \"value\" });\n```\n\n---\n\n## Key Takeaways\n\n1. **Partial v\u00e0 Required** l\u00e0 c\u1eb7p \u0111\u00f4i ho\u00e0n h\u1ea3o cho form handling v\u00e0 validation\n2. **Readonly** l\u00e0 must-have cho immutable patterns v\u00e0 configuration\n3. **Pick vs Omit** - ch\u1ecdn based on s\u1ed1 l\u01b0\u1ee3ng properties c\u1ea7n/b\u1ecf\n4. **Record** l\u00e0 go-to cho lookup tables v\u00e0 type-safe dictionaries\n5. **Exclude/Extract** powerful cho union manipulation\n6. **NonNullable** safety net sau validation\n7. **ReturnType** gi\u00fap DRY v\u00e0 type inference t\u1eeb functions\n8. **Composition** - combine utilities \u0111\u1ec3 t\u1ea1o complex types\n9. **Type Guards** - lu\u00f4n validate tr\u01b0\u1edbc khi use Required types\n10. **Naming Conventions** - \u0111\u1eb7t t\u00ean clear \u0111\u1ec3 express intent\n\n## K\u1ebft Lu\u1eadn\n\nTypeScript Utility Types kh\u00f4ng ch\u1ec9 l\u00e0 syntactic sugar - ch\u00fang l\u00e0 essential tools gi\u00fap b\u1ea1n vi\u1ebft type-safe code v\u1edbi less duplication v\u00e0 better maintainability. B\u1eb1ng c\u00e1ch master 10 utilities n\u00e0y, b\u1ea1n c\u00f3 th\u1ec3:\n\n- \u2705 Eliminate type duplication\n- \u2705 Build type-safe APIs v\u00e0 data layers\n- \u2705 Enforce immutability v\u00e0 correctness\n- \u2705 Create flexible, reusable type definitions\n- \u2705 Improve developer experience with better autocomplete\n\n**Next Steps:**\n\n1. Check official TypeScript documentation cho more utilities\n5.
